<div id="expander-1649652251" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1649652251" class="expand-control">

Pull Request

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1649652251" class="expand-content">

Author: [Ryan Kajiura](https://wiki.pinnacle.com/display/~ryank)

*Pull requests are an effective way to perform code review and
collaboration in a positive way in the team.*

## Pull requests offer

  - Complete diff (difference) of the changes to each file.
  - Automatic updates so you can see changes as they are made
  - Inline comments so you can pinpoint change suggestions
  - Tasks to help you keep track of what changes need attention
  - Notifications for comments, commits, or approvals
  - Two merge strategy options for Git repositories

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Pull Request Process**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

<div id="expander-1651718544" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1651718544" class="expand-control">

Build better Pull Requests

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1651718544" class="expand-content">

Here are a few suggestions to make PULL REQUESTS more effective.

  - Try to make the pull request small enough to review but large enough
    to give you the context of the feature, bug fix, or update
  - Use @mentions  and in-line comments to guide specific reviewers to
    specific items in the code
  - Ask reviewers to create TASKS for things which must be addressed for
    APPROVAL. This helps designate between suggestions and discussions
    and things which must be fixed
  - An accurate description and links to any issues gives reviewers more
    context and better access to what they need to understand the
    problem or feature you're addressing

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-868583591" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-868583591" class="expand-control">

Create a Pull Request

</div>

<div id="expander-content-868583591" class="expand-content">

### Option 1: Full Stash interface

1.  ACTIONS (left side menu) \> Click CREATE PULL REQUEST  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405735567.png)

2.  (**A**) Select Branch: Select the branch with the changes you want
    to merge

3.  (**B**) Select Source and Destination: From the drop down, check the
    destination repository and branch

4.  (**C**) Click CONTINUE  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405735568.png)

5.  (**D**) TITLE: Add a Title that is appropriate

6.  (**E**) DESCRIPTION: Add a Description that can be easily recognized
    (in notifications and the pull request list)

7.  (**F**) REVIEWERS: Start to type the reviewer's name and select it
    from the list provided in the automatic search

8.  (**G**) Click CREATE  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405735569.png)

**<span class="underline">Note</span>**

Select reviewers for this pull request to make key contributors aware of
the changes and create an effective review.

Every REVIEWER can COMMENT on the pull request, and with a single click
give their APPROVAL.

If changes are made to the code, they can see those changes as soon as
the new commit is made.

Additionally, the contributors you invite can decide to stop watching
the pull request with a simple click.

### Option 2: SourceTree

When you commit your feature branch to remote

Right click on the feature branch and click Create pull request....

![](attachments/405735527/426476109.png)

This will redirect you to Stash interface

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1358140015" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1358140015" class="expand-control">

Add Reviewers to your Pull Request

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1358140015" class="expand-content">

1\. Add a REVIEWER to the Pull Request when you create it by **(F1)**
typing their Bitbucket USER or EMAIL to the Reviewers section of the
page.

2\. And then click to **(F2)** select the desired name from the
automatic list of users.

![](attachments/405735527/405735579.png)  

3\. After you click to select the desired name, it will **(F3)**
automatically populate as one of the REVIEWERS.

![](attachments/405735527/405735580.png)

4\. Add more reviewer names as desired.

Note: You may also add REVIEWERS to the Pull Request after it is in
progress by clicking EDIT button (between *Merge* and *Decline*) at the
top of the request.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1413661048" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1413661048" class="expand-control">

Compare before issuing a Request

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1413661048" class="expand-content">

Before creating a Pull Request, you should compare your outgoing
Requests to the destination Repository.This tells you how much the
destination Repository changed while you were working on your fork or
branch. You do this by comparing incoming Changes.

→ It is good practice to make sure that there are no incoming changes
before you make your Pull Request.

If there are changes what do you do? It depends on your project
workflow. For example, if you are working on a team, your project
workflow might require you to MERGE and TEST incoming changes *before*
sending your outgoing changes back to the destination.

#### To compare your source to the destination, do the following.

1.  From the Repository with the changes, **(H1)** click  **...**  (top
    center) and **(H2)** select COMPARE  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405735627.png)  
    Bitbucket displays**(H3)** the *Compare *page.  
      
2.  Adjust the SOURCE and DESTINATION values so that they match the Pull
    Request you anticipate making.  
      
    a) Click to access**(H4)** the DIFF tab to see **(H5)** "There are
    no changes" (if there were no changes).  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405735607.png)  
      
    b) Click to access**(H6)** the COMMITS tab to see **(H7)** "There
    are no commits found" (if there were no commits)  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405735608.png)  
      
    c) Note:  If there are changes, you'll see a DIFF of the changes and
    a list of COMMITS.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-347234100" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-347234100" class="expand-control">

Request the destination Owner pull your changes

</div>

<div id="expander-content-347234100" class="expand-content">

**To create a Pull Request, do the following:**

1.  From the repository, in the ACTIONS sidebar select CREATE PULL
    REQUEST  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405735863.png)  
    Bitbucket displays the **(I1)** PULL REQUEST page.
2.  Use the drop down to **(I2)** Select Branch.
3.  Press **(I3)** CONTINUE. Note: The "Continue" button will not become
    available until you "Select Branch".  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405735873.png)
4.  Enter a **(I4)** TITLE and **(I5)** DESCRIPTION for your Pull
    Request.
5.  Add a **(I6)** REVIEWER
6.  Click **(I7)** CREATE  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405735875.png)
7.  The Pull Request is now created.

Note: Immediately in EMAIL and in STASH, the Reviewer will receive
NOTIFICATION that there is a new Pull Request.

To see the list of all the Pull Requests against this repository, you
can click **(I8)** PULL REQUESTS in the Navigation bar.

![](attachments/405735527/405735874.png)

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1282194132" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1282194132" class="expand-control">

Check Build Status on a Pull Request

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1282194132" class="expand-content">

If your vendor or build system runs a Build when you make a Commit, you
can see the Status of the Build(s) on each Commit.

After you create a Pull Request, its OVERVIEW tab includes the Build
Status for all the Commits on that Pull Request.

Click the COMMITS tab to see the Builds Statuses separated by Commits.

![](attachments/405735527/405736258.png)

The BUILDS column contains one of these statuses:

  - ![](https://confluence.atlassian.com/bitbucket/files/304578655/790630066/1/1447862298449/build_status_passed.png)appears
    if all builds for that commit passed  
  - ![](https://confluence.atlassian.com/bitbucket/files/304578655/790630067/1/1447862317670/build_status_progress.png)appears
    if no builds for that commit failed and at least one build is in
    progress  
  - ![](https://confluence.atlassian.com/bitbucket/files/304578655/790630068/1/1447862335598/build_status_failed.png)appears
    if at least one build for that commit failed  

From the COMMIT column, click the link to the Commit that you want to
see. 

On the right side of the COMMIT page, you see the BUILD STATUS icon
again and a link to MORE DETAILS.

  

Click the link to see MORE DETAILS of each Build for the Commit. 

The TABLE that opens when you click a BUILD STATUS includes only the
most recent status for each BUILD, not a History of Builds for the
Commit.

You can also check the BUILD STATUSES for a repository without creating
a PULL REQUEST.

To see the BUILD STATUS on a Commit, press COMMITS on the left side of
the repository.

![](attachments/405735527/405738292.png)

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-14909221" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-14909221" class="expand-control">

Accept a Pull Request

</div>

<div id="expander-content-14909221" class="expand-content">

Only a user with write permissions on the destination repository can
ACCEPT or REJECT a Pull Request.

Any user with read permission in a repository can REVIEW the list of
open, accepted and rejected Pull Requests. 

**The following procedure shows the steps to ACCEPT a Pull Request:**

1.  From your repository, click PULL REQUESTS in the sidebar.  
    A list of incoming Pull Requests display with the OPEN context. 
2.  On the list, click a Pull Request.  
    The Pull Request DETAILS appear and the VIEW defaults to the
    DIFF context.  
    You can also view the COMMITS or the Comment Activity on the
    request.  
    ![](attachments/405735527/405736259.png)
3.  Examine the request using the various contexts..
4.  If you decide that you want to Merge the Fork into your own
    repository, click MERGE.
5.  Confirm the action if prompted.   
    Bitbucket merges the changes into your repository, all on the
    Bitbucket server.

<div class="confluence-information-macro confluence-information-macro-information">

<span class="aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-info confluence-information-macro-icon"></span>

<div class="confluence-information-macro-body">

If an UPDATE PULL REQUEST button appears by a request, this means that
the fork changed after the Pull Request was sent.

You can click UPDATE PULL REQUEST to apply those changes to the Pull
Request.

Or, you can ACCEPT and PULL what is in the Request alone.

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-682493763" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-682493763" class="expand-control">

Merge a Pull Request

</div>

<div id="expander-content-682493763" class="expand-content">

Merging your changes is the final stage of the pull request process.

**Complete the following steps to merge a pull request:**

1.  Click the MERGE button.

You'll see something similar to the following screenshot.

![](attachments/405735527/405736263.png)

2\. (Optional) Update the COMMIT MESSAGE with more details.

3\. (For Git repositories only) Select a MERGE STRATEGY from the two
options:

  - MERGE COMMIT - Keeps all commits from your source branch and makes
    them part of the destination branch.  
    This option is the same as entering  **`git merge --no-ff`** in the
    command line.  
      
  - SQUASH - Combines your commits when you merge the source branch into
    the destination branch.  
    This option is the same as entering  **`git merge --squash`**  in
    the command line.  
      
    *→ For more details on these two types of merge strategies, refer to
    the rest of this section.*  

4\. (Optional) If you're merging two branches in the same repository,
you can select the CLOSE SOURCE BRANCH checkbox to remove the branch
from the list of repository branches.

5\. Click the MERGE button.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-806420136" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-806420136" class="expand-control">

Merge Checklist

</div>

<div id="expander-content-806420136" class="expand-content">

As you're about to Merge your Pull Request, you may see a MERGE
CHECKLIST

This Checklist is a list of items that your administrator requests that
you resolve *before you merge your code*.

Any checklist items with a
![(warning)](images/icons/emoticons/warning.png) are unresolved.

If your administrator requires that you resolve the items, you won't be
able to merge.

Otherwise, you can choose to ignore these warnings on the checklist and
merge anyway.

  

<div class="table-wrap">

| If this checklist item has a ![(warning)](images/icons/emoticons/warning.png) | Then your pull request...                                                |
| ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **At least {\#} approvals**                                                   | doesn't have that number of approvals                                    |
| **At least {\#} successful builds on last commit**                            | doesn't have that number of successful builds for the most recent commit |
| **No failed builds on last commit**                                           | has failed builds on the most recent commit                              |
| **Resolved pull request tasks**                                               | has open pull request tasks                                              |

</div>

  

![](attachments/405735527/405736231.png)

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1201432451" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1201432451" class="expand-control">

Merge Strategies

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1201432451" class="expand-content">

<div class="confluence-information-macro confluence-information-macro-information">

<span class="aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-info confluence-information-macro-icon"></span>

<div class="confluence-information-macro-body">

While merge strategies currently only apply to Git repositories, we're
planning to support them on Mercurial repositories in the future.

At the moment, clicking MERGE on a Mercurial pull request performs a
MERGE COMMIT.

</div>

</div>

Both strategies merge all your commits from your source branch to the
destination branch.

The type of strategy you chose to use depends on your team's workflow
and how you use your repository.

#### Strategy 1: When to do a Merge Commit

Select MERGE COMMIT when you want to maintain an exact history of
changes. Merge commits are also useful if, as part of your workflow,
pull requests are large in scope and you review commits
individually. Because this strategy keeps all commits during the merge,
you'll still see all commits from the source branch on the COMMITS page.

#### Strategy 2: When to do a Squash Merge

Select SQUASH to make your commits list less cluttered, which results
in less time to search for commits that introduce a bug (with a `git
bisect`) and provides an easy-to-follow commit history. Because this
strategy combines all commits when you merge, you'll only see one commit
on the destination branch on the COMMITS page.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-523339569" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-523339569" class="expand-control">

Revert a Pull Request

</div>

<div id="expander-content-523339569" class="expand-content">

While you can't undo a pull request, you can revert the merged commit
from a pull request if necessary.

Bitbucket takes two steps to revert a pull request:

1\) Bitbucket creates a new branch with one commit that reverses the
merged commit.

2) Bitbucket creates a new pull request for the branch and commit.

  

**To Revert a Pull Request**

1.  From the pull request, click the REVERT button in the top right.

2.  (Optional) From the REVERT PULL REQUEST dialog, change the BRANCH
    NAME for the new branch you're about to create.

3.  Click the REVERT button.  
    **NOTE**:  Once you click REVERT, Bitbucket creates the new branch.
    Even if you CANCEL the pull request, the revert branch remains in
    the repository.

4.  The CREATE A PULL REQUEST page opens with the revert branch as the
    source.  
    After you add your reviewers and make additional changes, click
    CREATE.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1799598723" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1799598723" class="expand-control">

Decline a Pull Request

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1799598723" class="expand-content">

Declining a pull request is the same as saying you don't want to ever
merge the changes in that pull request in their current state.

Any reviewer can decline a pull request so your team might want to
establish a policy about when to decline verses when to leave the pull
request open in a stagnant state.

**NOTE**: Declining a pull request cannot be undone. Once you decline a
pull request you will have to open a new pull request request to
continue a review. Declining a pull request has no effect on the
branches (source or destination) so the changes in the source branch are
still in that source branch.

To decline a pull request, navigate to the Pull Request and click the
DECLINE button (top left of the page).

**To view a declined pull request**

1.  From your repository, click PULL REQUESTS (in the sidebar).
2.  At the top, select the third tab DECLINED
3.  Select the desired Declined Pull Request

The comments and tasks in a pull request are preserved after it is
declined. 

You can add more comments to a declined pull request, however, new
changes pushed to the branch will no longer update the pull request.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-893082991" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-893082991" class="expand-control">

Resolve a Pull Request with Conflicts

</div>

<div id="expander-content-893082991" class="expand-content">

When it detects Conflicts in a pull request's incoming code, Bitbucket
cannot automatically Accept and Merge.

If this happens, Bitbucket notifies you and instructs you how to
proceed when you click MERGE.

![](attachments/405735527/405736268.png)

1.  **Source and destination:** The source repository and branch name
    points to the destination branch name.
2.  **Conflict instructions:** Use these instructions to merge locally. 

To resolve these kinds of conflicts, you pull the changes to your local
repository and resolve them there.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-858332292" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-858332292" class="expand-control">

Manually Merge Pull Requests locally

</div>

<div id="expander-content-858332292" class="expand-content">

Sometimes, it is a good idea to use a workflow where you test a change
set on your local system before accepting a pull request.

You can do this with any pull request.

**The typical workflow is this**.

  - Receive a pull request in Bitbucket
  - Update your local repository with the incoming change set
  - Investigate and/or test the change set

→If you the change set is good, you merge it into your local repository.

You may have to resolve some conflicts. Then, you push the local
repository back to Bitbucket. Back on Bitbucket, the pull request is
marked as accepted in the PULL REQUESTS tab.

→ If you don't like the change request, you discard the changes locally
and reject the pull request on Bitbucket.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1576588231" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1576588231" class="expand-control">

Git Command Line example

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1576588231" class="expand-content">

<div class="table-wrap">

<table>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p>This is a simple Git example of the procedure for pulling changes made by another user from a fork of a Bitbucket repository, back into the original repository also on Bitbucket.</p>

<li><p>Check for incoming changes <em>(one change detected)</em></p>

 adding images</code></pre></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</div></li>

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Pull Request Process**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

<div id="expander-856633167" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-856633167" class="expand-control">

Clear and concise title

</div>

<div id="expander-content-856633167" class="expand-content">

Code reviewers will skim the title of the change to decide if they want
to review the code and if so, when. So let's make this easy for them.

**Keep the title short, but expressive enough to signal what the
reviewer can expect.**Let's say you're working on an accounting software
and there is a new business requirement on how to calculate tax for
Switzerland. A title like`Changes for Swiss tax calculation`is concise.
A title like`Change for tax calculation in Switzerland for new
regulation`is still concise, with more context. However, a title
like`Adding new tax parameters`or`Change tax logic`are overly generic
and won't help reviewers give an idea of the type of change. This will
make it difficult for them to decide if they should review the change.
What about titles like`TaxInternals structure update and
CalculateEffectiveRate changes in case of Swiss country code` or `Change
tax calculation for Swiss businesses in the TX bracket effective
from 2019 following new regulation`? These are on the other end of the
spectrum: they are verbose and feel they provide like too much detail in
the title. What is too little and what is too much information will
depend on your environment: try to strike the right balance.

As the team grows, it can make sense to agree on conventions to make
titles easy to compare. One practice, for example, that my team have
adopted is starting the title with uppercase and the first word being a
verb in present tense. So we prefer`Change Swiss tax calculation for new
regulation`over`changed Swiss tax calculation for new
regulation` or `Ability to calculate Swiss tax for new regulation`.
This kind of suggestion can be a nice touch for consistency across code
reviews or onboarding new people - but all of it will be specific to
your team or company.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-910085780" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-910085780" class="expand-control">

The "why" of the change

</div>

<div id="expander-content-910085780" class="expand-content">

People reviewing the code spend a lot less time thinking about the
change as the author. Providing the context in the description of the
change request helps them up to speed on the reasoning behind the code
changes.

**Having a clear "why" section will make the code easier to review for
people for everyone.**For people with plenty of domain knowledge, it
serves as a quick validation and they will verify if you follow what you
set out to. For people with less domain knowledge - such as recent team
members or people not familiar with the codebase - it will allow to do a
decent review. Having people who are not that familiar with the codebase
can both bring in a new perspective and it is also an efficient way to
share knowledge.

For teams using project management tools, on top of a short and clear
description, linking to the tracking task is helpful. The task often has
a lot more context, often conversations and can help the curious
reviewer dig deeper and catch up on context. The same goes for linking
other resources that can help understand the "why" deeper, such as
design documents.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-620176215" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-620176215" class="expand-control">

Visual support

</div>

<div id="expander-content-620176215" class="expand-content">

For client-side changes, such as those on the web or mobile, few things
make a review easier than attaching "before" and "after" screenshots -
gifs or video recordings for changes on animations.

This is a practice that not only helps the reviewers greatly, but also
the author, who does another verification when creating the pull
request. For changes impacting the UI, without this visual aid, thorough
reviewers would have to grab the changes, build the product and run it
in their local environment to visualize the changes.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-596288984" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-596288984" class="expand-control">

Pull request guides and best practices for your team

</div>

<div id="expander-content-596288984" class="expand-content">

My team came up with code review request best practices that we
circulated, reviewed and committed to and now use it to onboard new
members. This was a good exercise to decide what things we cared about,
as a team, and to turn best practices into*our*practices.

One thing that worked especially well was having a list of a few,
internal examples of code review requests that were deemed easy to
review. Good code review requests come in different shapes and sizes.
Having best practices helps set team-level expectations. Good

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

Reviewer.

![](attachments/405740677/419990510.png)

changeset.

![](attachments/405740677/419990513.png)

  

Click the Diff tab, you can see the difference between previous version
and current version. At this point you have the option to Reject or
Approve the changes.

![](attachments/405740677/419990514.png)

You also have the ability to view the full source

![](attachments/405740677/419990515.png)

  

### Approve

After you Approve the pull request you can merge the changes back to
Master.

![](attachments/405740677/419990516.png)

  

After you Merge you will see a the status here.

![](attachments/405740677/419990519.png)

### Reject

When you Reject the request. You do have the ability to add feedback.

![](attachments/405740677/419990527.png)

  

Email will be sent to the Pull Request initiator

![](attachments/405740677/419990521.png)

Bitbucket will also display the Rejection notification

![](attachments/405740677/419990522.png)

Pull Request Process to merge your Feature branch back to develop branch

  

Finished Feature in Git-Flow. 

  - Uncheck Rebase on development branch and Delete branch

![](attachments/423266600/426475653.png)

  

  

Create Release branch, after package has been deployed to production
environment, Finished Release in Git-Flow.

  - Uncheck Delete branch
  - option to set a tag
  - option to directly push changes to remote

![](attachments/423266600/426475654.png)

  

Click on the Git-flow

![](attachments/423266600/423267576.png)

  

Click on Finish the type of branch

![](attachments/423266600/423268039.png)

  

In this cause you'll see where the branch will be merged to. Make sure
you have checked marked delete branch, this will only remove it locally
from your repository. Then click OK.

Note: This will auto merge your branch to the designated branch(s)
depending on which type of branch (Feature/ Release or Hotfix) you where
working on.  

![](attachments/423266600/423268040.png)

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Administration Configuration**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

<div id="expander-1740984046" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1740984046" class="expand-control">

Git ignore File

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1740984046" class="expand-content">

The .gitignore file is a text file that tells Git which files or folders
to ignore in a project.  
A local .gitignore file is usually placed in the root directory of a
project. You can also create a global .gitignore file and any entries in
that file will be ignored in all of your Git repositories.  
To create a local .gitignore file, create a text file and name it
.gitignore (remember to include the . at the beginning). Then edit this
file as needed. Each new line should list an additional file or folder
that you want Git to ignore.  
The entries in this file can also follow a matching pattern.

  - `*` is used as a wildcard match
  - `/` is used to ignore pathnames relative to the .gitignore file
  - `#` is used to add comments to a .gitignore file

  

Master reference template can be found here

  - <https://github.com/github/gitignore>
  - <https://github.com/github/gitignore/blob/master/VisualStudio.gitignore>

  

This company uses multiple coding languages. I have consolidated the
main languages to a single page. The page is broke down in these
sections

  - DotNet
  - Java
  - Custom specific for the project

  

When updating the file. Remember not to replace all.

[![](rest/documentConversion/latest/conversion/thumbnail/446665827/1)](/download/attachments/423266600/git-ignore-dotnet.txt?version=1&modificationDate=1554118977313&api=v2)[![](rest/documentConversion/latest/conversion/thumbnail/446665828/1)](/download/attachments/423266600/git-ignore-java.txt?version=1&modificationDate=1554118977497&api=v2)[![](rest/documentConversion/latest/conversion/thumbnail/446665829/1)](/download/attachments/423266600/git-ignore-all.txt?version=1&modificationDate=1554118977653&api=v2)

  

  

</div>

<div id="expander-471415838" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-471415838" class="expand-control">

Project & Repository Settings

</div>

<div id="expander-content-471415838" class="expand-content">

### Post Creation of New Project

1.  Branch permissions configured to the people who are the Default
    Reviewers for the project the repository is under
    1.  Project Settings \> Branch Permissions \> Add Permissions
        1.  branch develop
        2.  check Prevent changes without a pull request, excepted by:  
2.  <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);">Merge
    checks</span></span>
    1.  Project Settings \> Merge Checks \> enable Minimum approvals
3.  <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);">Merge
    strategies</span></span>
    1.  Project Settings \> Merge Strategies \> enable Merge commit
4.  <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);">Default
    Reviewers</span></span>
    1.  <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);"><span style="color: rgb(51,51,0);">Project
        Settings \> Default Reviewers \> Add default
        reviewers</span></span>
        1.  Source branch: Any branch
        2.  Target branch: Any branch
        3.  Default Reviewers: teams leads and managers. See Default
            Reviewers below.
        4.  Approvals required: 1  

### Post Creation of New Repository

Most configuration should be inheriting from Project configuration.

1.  Set the default branch to
    <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">develop</span>
    1.  Repository Settings \> Repository Details \> Default Branch

### Security

#### Branch Permissions

  - Add permission  
    Note: make sure <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">Develop branch
    has been created  
    </span>
      - Select Develop branch
      - check <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">Prevent changes without
        a pull request, except by:  
        </span>
          - Leave empty

<div id="expander-1467262579" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1467262579" class="expand-control">

Database Project - Folder Structure

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1467262579" class="expand-content">

Source control will have these folders

![](attachments/423266600/446665038.png)

  

### DataChanges

Any data changes required during deployment. All Insert statements needs
to be idempotent

### Functions

A programming construct that accepts parameters, does work that
typically makes use of the accepted parameters, and returns a type of
result.

Each Function should be in its own file and idempotent. Do not use Alter
statement, always use Create.

![](attachments/423266600/446665039.png)

  

### SchemaChanges

Any table changes required during deployment. All changes needs to be
idempotent.

![](attachments/423266600/446665040.png)

> ref: <https://gist.github.com/kmoormann/3758257>

### Sequence

A sequence is a user-defined schema bound object that generates a
sequence of numeric values according to the specification with which the
sequence was created. The sequence of numeric values is generated in an
ascending or descending order at a defined interval and can be
configured to restart (cycle) when exhausted. Sequences, unlike identity
columns, are not associated with specific tables.

Each Sequence should be in its own file and idempotent. Do not use Alter
statement, always use Create.

![](attachments/423266600/446665041.png)

### Stored Procedures

Consolidate and centralize logic that was originally implemented in
applications

![](attachments/423266600/446665042.png)

Each Stored Procedure should be in its own file and idempotent. Do not
use Alter statement, always use Create.

### Triggers

SQL Code that will automatically executes when an event occurs in the
database server

![](attachments/423266600/446665043.png)

Each Stored Procedure should be in its own file and idempotent. Do not
use Alter statement, always use Create.

### Types - Table

Parameters to send multiple rows of data to a Transact-**SQL** statement
or a routine

![](attachments/423266600/446665044.png)

Each Type - Table should be in its own file and idempotent. Do not use
Alter statement, always use Create.

### Views

Aa searchable object in a database that is defined by a query

![](attachments/423266600/446665045.png)

Each View should be in its own file and idempotent. Do not use Alter
statement, always use Create.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1108024981" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1108024981" class="expand-control">

Transfering Git Database

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1108024981" class="expand-content">

Author: [Ryan Kajiura](https://wiki.pinnacle.com/display/~ryank)

Git is nowadays the*de fact*o standard in version control, distributed
or not. It comes with a vast array of powerful features, some of them go
unnoticed by the majority of its casual users. One such feature is Git’s
capability to connect your local repository with multiple remote
repositories, as well as removing and adding remote locations as you
wish.

  

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Git Remotes**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

In contrast to older version control tools, such as CVS and SVN, where
all code was centralised in a single repository, Git allows code to
co-exist in an unlimited number of remote repositories.In fact, the mere
notion of the original, central, or “origin”, repository in Git is just
a convention. It just*happens*to be the repository most users started
synchronising with when they did that initial`git clone`. As the project
progresses repository location and preferences may change, so what was
once, in the beginning, the*origin*may start to seem irrelevant:

![](https://miro.medium.com/max/3538/1*2jIXuOz2ML1rr_5A7hU2Pw.png)

Remotes can be introduced at will in Git (image by author)

</div>

</div>

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Transferring Method**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

We’ve established so far that you can have as many remotes as you wish
and that their name doesn’t have any significant role in Git’s
ecosystem. So, how can we leverage this feature of Git to transfer files
from one remote to another?

## Losing all history (developer-god mode)

The quick and dirty way is to just clone the new, empty repository,
copy/paste the files from the source repository, and commit/push.
Although that approach might save you a few minutes and doesn’t require
any other than the standard Git commands you already know, it comes with
a severe drawback.Since you are the one committing all the files to the
new repository, you are now becoming the sole author of every single
file of the source repository. Any previous commit history, kept in the
source repository, is now lost forever and the whole project looks like
it has been created by a single person (you).Developer-god syndrome
satisfied; original authors pissed off.

## Keeping history

Copying resources from one repository to another while keeping commit
history intact not only acknowledges everybody else’s original work but
might come with useful perks. For example, you can search previous
commit messages to find an explication that sheds light into an issue
you’re investigating; if you realise a specific developer is prone to
the same type of mistakes, you can easily filter out his/her commits to
re-check them, and many more.

<div id="expander-1014930056" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1014930056" class="expand-control">

Transfer Commands

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1014930056" class="expand-content">

If you search for how to transfer a Git repository you’ll end up with
several different suggestions, ranging from simple sequences of Git
commands to pure Git black magic.

The approach suggested next may not necessarily be “the best out there”,
however, it has been tested on repositories with thousands of commits
and is honouring two basic principles: 1/ Keeping the complete commit
history including all branches and tags, and 2/ not interfering with the
original repository.

So, let’s start with the commands.

## Start by creating a mirrored clone of your old repository

> git clone --mirror old-repo-url new-repo

Replace`old-repo-url`with the Git URL of your old repo and give an
appropriate name to the`new-repo`folder on which it will be cloned.

## Remove the remote reference to the original/old repository

> cd new-repo  
> git remote remove origin

You may get a warning if your original repository contains branches but
you can ignore it. Technically speaking, this step is not necessary
since as discussed above you can have multiple remotes, however, it
makes future commands a bit simpler to type and completely detaches you
from the original repository.

## Add the remote reference for the new repository

> git remote add origin new-repo-url

Replace`new-repo-url`with the Git URL of your new repository. It goes
without saying that you should have had the new repo created beforehand
in your favourite Git management system.

## Push everything to the new repository

> git push --all  
> git push --tags

## Clone the new repository

> cd ..  
> rm -rf new-repo  
> git clone new-repo-url new-repo

Replace`new-repo-url`and`new-repo`with your new repository.

This last step is necessary because the clone performed in step (1) was
a mirrored clone that can’t be used as such for further commits. Let me
know in the comments if you’re aware of a way to convert it, effectively
bypassing this re-cloning step.

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-control-2046549686" class="expand-control">

Coding

</div>

<div id="expander-content-254966858" class="expand-content">

<div class="confluence-information-macro has-no-icon confluence-information-macro-information">

<div class="confluence-information-macro-body">

![(info)](images/icons/emoticons/information.svg) Selenium

Selenium is designed to automate web browser interaction, so scripts can
automatically perform the same interactions that any user can perform
manually. Selenium can perform any sort of automated interaction, but
was originally intended and is primarily used for automated web
application testing. 

</div>

</div>

  

<div class="table-wrap">

<table>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>The Seven Basic Steps of Selenium Tests</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Create a WebDriver instance.</li>
<li>Navigate to a Web page.</li>
<li>Locate an HTML element on the Web page.</li>
<li>Perform an action on an HTML element.</li>
<li>Anticipate the browser response to the action.</li>
<li>Run tests and record test results using a test framework.</li>
<li>Conclude the test.</li>
</ol></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</div>

## Project Structure:

  

base (Parent folder of pom packaging, only contains pom.xml's of
children folders, also contains the parent pom.xml which lists all
dependencies) 

\-----helper (Child of base folder with type jar packaging, contains a
library of code applicable to any new website module) 

\-----websites (Child of base folder with type pom packaging, only
contains pom.xml's of it's children folders, and it's own pom.xml file
lists the helper folder as a dependency)

\---------------Arcadia (Child of website folder with jar type
packaging, only contains code related to the arcadia website)

\---------------AtaTransferTool (Child of website folder with jar type
packaging, only contains code related to the ATATransferTool website)

\---------------LanPages (Child of website folder with jar type
packaging, only contains code related to the LanPages website)

  

## Getting Started, Creating a Module For a New Website 

1.  Navigate to the "websites" folder in eclipse
2.  Right click on the "websites" folder
3.  Click new→other
4.  Click on Maven→Maven Module→Next
5.  Check off "Create a simple project (skip archetype selection)
6.  Enter the website name in the "Module Name:" input box
7.  Make sure "Parent Project" is "websites"
8.  click Next-\>Finish

## How to Create a Basic Automated Test Case in Selenium

1.  Navigate to folder websitename→src/test/java
2.  right click on src/test/java 
3.  create a new class
4.  right click on base then click Maven→Update Maven Project-\>Ok
5.  import the following code into the new class: and add  "extends
    TestBase" in your class declaration:  
    ![](attachments/423266835/444564899.png)
6.  Initialize variables:  
    ![](attachments/423266835/444564900.png)
7.  Create and initialize the following base methods:   
    ![](attachments/423266835/444564978.png)  
    \*Note: if the website you want to go to is not already in the
    config file, then go to
    helper-\>src/main/java-\>com.qa.config→config.properties and add
    your website link in 
8.  Create a basic test method and place it between the @BeforeMethod
    and @AfterMethod:  
    ![](attachments/423266835/444564979.png)
9.  Create a test ng file:  
    right click folder (your test website's folder)  
    click on file  
    enter name: testng.xml  
    press ok  
    navigate to testng.xml  
    paste the following code:  
    ![](attachments/423266835/444565015.png)  
    \*Note: fill in parameter values based on your needs
10. Now that everything is setup, run your test by right clicking your
    website's folder name in eclipse and clicking run as maven
    install   
      
    \*Note: the expected output should be your website link being opened
    in chrome, and "hey" being outputted in the console

<div id="expander-1415762718" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1415762718" class="expand-control">

Automation Standard

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1415762718" class="expand-content">

Author:  [Ryan Kajiura](https://wiki.pinnacle.com/display/~ryank)

  

Production-ready software requires testing before it goes into
production. As the discipline of software development matured, software
testing approaches have matured too. Instead of having myriads of manual
software testers, development teams have moved towards automating the
biggest portion of their testing efforts. Automating their tests allows
teams to know whether their software is broken in a matter of seconds
and minutes instead of days and weeks.

The drastically shortened feedback loop fuelled by automated tests goes
hand in hand with agile development practices, continuous delivery and
DevOps culture. Having an effective software testing approach allows
teams to move fast and with confidence.

![](https://www.simform.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Untitled-design-4.png)

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Importance of Test Automation**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

Software has become an essential part of the world we live in. It has
outgrown its early sole purpose of making businesses more efficient.
Today companies try to find ways to become first-class digital
companies. As users everyone of us interacts with an ever-increasing
amount of software every day. The wheels of innovation are turning
faster.

If you want to keep pace you'll have to look into ways to deliver your
software faster without sacrificing its quality.**Continuous delivery**,
a practice where you automatically ensure that your software can be
released into production any time, can help you with that. With
continuous delivery you use a**build pipeline**to automatically test
your software and deploy it to your testing and production environments.

Building, testing and deploying an ever-increasing amount of software
manually soon becomes impossible — unless you want to spend all your
time with manual, repetitive work instead of delivering working
software. Automating everything — from build to tests, deployment and
infrastructure — is your only way forward.

![](https://martinfowler.com/articles/practical-test-pyramid/buildPipeline.png)

Figure 1: Use build pipelines to automatically and reliably get your
software into production

Traditionally software testing was overly manual work done by deploying
your application to a test environment and then performing some
black-box style testing e.g. by clicking through your user interface to
see if anything's broken. Often these tests would be specified by test
scripts to ensure the testers would do consistent checking.

It's obvious that testing all changes manually is time-consuming,
repetitive and tedious. Repetitive is boring, boring leads to mistakes
and makes you look for a different job by the end of the week.

Luckily there's a remedy for repetitive tasks:*automation*.

Automating your repetitive tests can be a big game changer in your life
as a software developer. Automate these tests and you no longer have to
mindlessly follow click protocols in order to check if your software
still works correctly. Automate your tests and you can change your
codebase without batting an eye. If you've ever tried doing a
large-scale refactoring without a proper test suite I bet you know what
a terrifying experience this can be. How would you know if you
accidentally broke stuff along the way? Well, you click through all your
manual test cases, that's how. But let's be honest: do you really enjoy
that? How about making even large-scale changes and knowing whether you
broke stuff within seconds while taking a nice sip of coffee? Sounds
more enjoyable if you ask me.

  

The figure shows the initial time & efforts it takes in learning the
best practices of test automation. But we can see how it saves the
overall effort and time spent.  

![TestAutomationStrategiesGraph](https://www.simform.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/TestAutomationStrategiesGraph.png)

  

</div>

</div>

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Test Pyramid**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

Test Pyramid is a great visual metaphor telling you to think about
different layers of testing. It also tells you how much testing to do on
each layer.

Stick to the pyramid shape to come up with a healthy, fast and
maintainable test suite: Write*lots*of small and fast*unit tests*.
Write*some*more coarse-grained tests and*very few*high-level tests that
test your application from end to end. Watch out that you don't end up
with a[test ice-cream
cone](https://watirmelon.blog/testing-pyramids/)that will be a nightmare
to maintain and takes way too long to run.

Don't become too attached to the names of the individual layers in
Cohn's test pyramid. In fact they can be quite misleading:*service
test*is a term that is hard to grasp (Cohn himself talks about the
observation that[a lot of developers completely ignore this
layer](https://www.mountaingoatsoftware.com/blog/the-forgotten-layer-of-the-test-automation-pyramid)).
In the days of single page application frameworks like react, angular,
ember.js and others it becomes apparent that*UI tests*don't have to be
on the highest level of your pyramid - you're perfectly able to unit
test your UI in all of these frameworks.

  

  

![](https://miro.medium.com/max/1092/0*q2maW8NjQFPvzZPL)![](attachments/412713262/446666626.png)

  

**Legends**

  - Colors: does not have any meaning
  - The size of the diamond face represents the test coverage in each
    phase
  - On the left, there is a hypothesis of test type (change it to fit
    needs)
  - Some other type of test like performance, stability, soak, code
    validation, security investigations, infrastructure checks, … should
    be added.

Automated Test should cover mostly critical functionalities (for example
the Order Flow, the Customer Care channels, the delivery process, ….)
and must cover deep investigations on the visible User interface and in
the invisible backend systems, databases, virtual environments,
integration with external systems, …

It is not an easy job\! It cannot be done only by a traditional test
gate.

Confidence in testing can be eroded by doubts: are we testing the right
things, are a test-set at the proper coverage, are the integration tests
executes in production-like setup, and so on. As mitigation we can:

  - At the Planning phase, decide which is the minimum set of test that
    has to be passed to declare the work done and ready for the next
    stage.
  - During each DevOps stage to look at the set of test and fill any gap
    or modify test things
  - At the Release stage (if using the Release on-demand) someone has
    the duty to approve the Deployment. He/She need a clear and
    synthetic view of the test results. So, taking track of all the
    testing results is crucial.
  - Reporting of historical results and their comparisons help in
    improvements
  - Learn from Production exceptions
  - On some stages, it is crucial to simulate some behavior (an
    integrated service is not available, not ready, unstable, under
    maintenance or not reachable), a service virtualization solution
    should help in doing things faster and with confidence. My thoughts
    are here…

## Eye of Providence

  

![Automated Testing Pyramid with
Eye](https://watirmelon.files.wordpress.com/2018/02/automated-testing-pyramid-with-eye.jpg?w=840)

## Testing Cloud

![Ideal Automated Testing
Pyramid.jpg](https://watirmelon.files.wordpress.com/2018/02/ideal-automated-testing-pyramid.jpg?w=840)

  

</div>

</div>

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Anti Pattern**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

## Ice-cream Cone

![Software Testing Icecream Cone
Antipattern](https://watirmelon.files.wordpress.com/2018/02/software-testing-icecream-cone-antipattern.jpg?w=840)

  

  

</div>

</div>

    automation](https://medium.com/@davide.cilano/agility-in-it-development-requires-the-use-of-test-automation-d11503db3508)
  - [Watirmelon - Testing
    pyramids](https://watirmelon.blog/testing-pyramids/)
  - [Martin Fowler - Practical test
    pyramid](https://martinfowler.com/articles/practical-test-pyramid.html)
  - [Simform - test automation
    strategy](https://www.simform.com/test-automation-strategy/)

<div id="expander-745374863" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-745374863" class="expand-control">

Team City

</div>

<div id="expander-content-745374863" class="expand-content">

Author: [Ryan Kajiura](https://wiki.pinnacle.com/display/~ryank)

  

Continuous Integration (CI) is the process of automating the build and
testing of code every time a team member commits changes to version
control. CI encourages developers to share their code and unit tests by
merging their changes into a shared version control repository after
every small task completion. Committing code triggers an automated build
system to grab the latest code from the shared repository and to build,
test, and validate the full master branch (also known as the trunk or
main).

CI emerged as a best practice because software developers often work in
isolation, and then they need to integrate their changes with the rest
of the team’s code base. Waiting days or weeks to integrate code creates
many merge conflicts, hard to fix bugs, diverging code strategies, and
duplicated efforts. CI requires the development team’s code be merged to
a shared version control branch continuously to avoid these problems.

CI keeps the master branch clean. Teams can leverage modern version
control systems such as Git to create short-lived feature branches to
isolate their work. A developer submits a “pull request” when the
feature is complete and, on approval of the pull request, the changes
get merged into the master branch. Then the developer can delete the
previous feature branch. Development teams repeat the process for
additional work. The team can establish branch policies to ensure the
master branch meets desired quality criteria.

Teams use build definitions to ensure that every commit to the master
branch triggers the automated build and testing processes. Implementing
CI this way ensures bugs are caught earlier in the development cycle,
which makes them less expensive to fix. Automated tests run for every
build to ensure builds maintain a consistent quality.

  

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelContent">

<div id="expander-961214410" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-961214410" class="expand-control">

Build Configuration Template

</div>

<div id="expander-content-961214410" class="expand-content">

All parameters (Configuration and Environment) variables are inherited
from the template level. Some variables can be overridden.

<span class="underline">Please understand Team City project Hierarchy
before making changes to variables.</span>

<span class="underline">  
</span>

<div id="expander-1913419144" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1913419144" class="expand-control">

Configuration Parameters

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1913419144" class="expand-content">

<div class="table-wrap">

| Parameter Name        | Description                                                                                              | Parameter is for this code base |
| --------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------- |
| AssembleyInfoFilePath | Relative path (from the root of location of Stash) to the AssembleyInfo file location.                   | C\#                             |
| BuildConfiguration    | Same as Visual Studio Build Configuration selection                                                      | C\#                             |
| BuildOutputDirectory  | Create a folder where the publish package will be created for packaging                                  | C\#                             |
| BuildTarget           | Same as Visual Studio Target configuration selection                                                     | C\#                             |
| OctopusChannel        | Octopus channel name where the build package will stored.                                                | C\#                             |
| OctopusEnvironment    | Octopus Environment is in reference to Octopus Lifecycle                                                 | C\#                             |
| OctopusPackagePath    | Nuget package that will be pushed to Octopus.                                                            | C\#                             |
| OctopusProjectName    | Octopus Project name Team City is associated to                                                          | C\#                             |
| SolutionName          | Visual Studio solution name                                                                              | C\#                             |
| TestFileNames         | Relative path (from the root of location of Stash) to the C\# and/or DLL that the Unit Test will execute | C\#                             |
| workspaceId           | part of the build package naming convention                                                              | JavaScript                      |
| workspaceNumber       | Build format number                                                                                      | JavaScript                      |

</div>

<td>Used for Code Analysis and Duplicate finder engine. Identify the version of Visual Studio. [ Build Solution step should correlate with exe arguments for Code Analysis and Code Duplicate Finder ]  <strong>(Not able to override)</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td>ToolsetVisualStudio2015</td>
<td>Used for Code Analysis and Duplicate finder engine. Identify the version of Visual Studio. [ Build Solution step should correlate with exe arguments for Code Analysis and Code Duplicate Finder ]  <strong>(Not able to override)</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>ToolsetVisualStudio2017</td>
<td>Used for Code Analysis and Duplicate finder engine. Identify the version of Visual Studio. [ Build Solution step should correlate with exe arguments for Code Analysis and Code Duplicate Finder ]  <strong>(Not able to override)</strong></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1843205350" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1843205350" class="expand-control">

Custom Scripts

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1843205350" class="expand-content">

All custom scripts are stored within an external PowerShell script. This
ensures consistent behavior in all build configuration and easier to
manage changes on a global scale.

  - CrescendoBuildsScripts.ps1  
    Centralize Custom script
  - CrescendoSendEmail.ps1  
    Generic function to send emails and attachments
  - DeploymentDebuggingLogs.ps1  
    Generic function to list all target server information.  This is
    being called in CrescendoBuildsScripts.ps1

  

Each agent host the scripts at the root of the buildAgent folder. The
scripts are programmatically deployed to all build agents with \_Update
TC Prod Server Scripts.ps1.

  

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

Build Template and Build Steps

</div>

<div id="expander-content-2107952740" class="expand-content">

<div id="expander-605111985" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-605111985" class="expand-control">

ITDev - BuildTemplate - Back End (VS 2015)

</div>

<div id="expander-content-605111985" class="expand-content">

1.  Deployment Debugging Logs - File  
    Generic function that will output all variables during the build.
    Will only be shown in the build logs.
2.  Nuget Installer  
    Nuget is the package manager for .NET.  A central package repository
    to allow other projects to reuse components
3.  Update Build Number from Assembly Info  
    Appends Team City build number to the projects package version
4.  SonarQuebe - Install TypeScript  
    Install TypeScript locally for SonarQube process
5.  SonarQube Runner  
    Set parameters to run code analysis
6.  SonarScanner for MSBuild: Being Analysis  
    Start scanning code base
7.  Build Solution  
    Build .NET solution
8.  C\# Unit Test  
    Run Unit Test
9.  Code Coverage  
    Generate code coverage report based on Unit Test results.
10. SonarScanner for MSBuild: Finish Analysis  
    Stop scanning code base
11. OctopusDeploy: Metadata - Git issue Tracking  
    List the changes contained in the release
12. OctopusDeploy: Metadata - Jira issue Tracking  
    List the changes contained in the release
13. OctopusDeploy: Push Package  
    Push build package to Octopus built-in repository
14. OctopusDeploy: Create Release  
    Deploy build package to defined target environment. It will be only
    the first environment within the Octopus defined LifeCycle
15. Email CI Report  
    Send email the team's slack channel as well as managers inbox.  
    Information provided:

<!-- end list -->

  -   - URL to SonarQube Code Analysis Report for the project
      - Team City build agent build ran on
      - Project Name
      - Build configuration
      - Build package version
      - who trigger the build
      - Attachments
          - Code Coverage trace log
          - Code Coverage report
          - SonarQuebe log
          - Unit Test test results  
              
              

</div>

Project Hierarchy

</div>

<div id="expander-content-157483021" class="expand-content">

![](attachments/411468885/412713373.png)

  

Using the screen shot above that list the Project in Team City.

Level 1 - Lets refer to as Team Level (ie... Apex, Arcadia, Customer,
....)

Level 2 - Lets refer to as Team Projects (ie..AccessControlAPI,
AccountAPI, AccountBackgroundService, ...)

Level 3 - Lets refer to as Build Configurations (ie.. Build Develop,
Build Release...)

  

#### Level 1

Configuration Parameters by default is not set.

Environment Variables is inherited. This would be a good location to
make changes to evn.SMTPTo. All Level 2 & 3 will receive notifications.

#### Level 2

Configuration Parametersby default is not set.  

Environment Variables is inherited.

#### Level 3

Configuration Parameters where you configure  

Environment Variables is inherited.

Good location to set the Default template and/or creating a new Build
Configuration  

![](attachments/411468885/411468891.png)

You can apply a template to existing Build Configurations

![](attachments/411468885/411468892.png)

![](attachments/411468885/411468893.png)

<div id="expander-1839384808" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1839384808" class="expand-control">

Create New Project Build Configuration

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1839384808" class="expand-content">

1.  Go to the proper Project/Sub-project location you want your builds
    to be located
2.  click on Create build configuration button
3.  click Manually configuration
4.  ensure Advance options are showing
5.  assign <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">Name to build
    configuration. Default build configuration names are:  
    </span>
    1.  Develop: Build Develop
    2.  Release: Build Release
6.  Select Based on template to correspond to your projects.
7.  Fill out the empty fields
8.  Select value if you see \< \> within the textbox. Options are
    proivded  
    Example:  
    \< Development | CI ( Quality Assurance ) \> - means you have either
    Development or CI ( Quality Assurance ) option
9.  Do not make any values changes within the actual step. Everything
    should be driven off the parameters

  

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1246049732" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1246049732" class="expand-control">

Version Control Settings (VCS)

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1246049732" class="expand-content">

For each build configuration VCS needs to be configured.

From the left navigation

1.  click on Version Control Settings
2.  Click the button Attach VCS root
3.  If you are creating a new project. Select from the Create new VCS
    root drop down list Git

## Develop

### Build configuration - VCS page

Under the Additional Options

  - **VCS checkout mode:**Always checkout files on server
  - **Checkout directory:**Auto (recommended)
  - **Clean Build:** Check Delete all files in the checkout directory
    before the build
  - **default branch settings:** Check Allow builds in the default
    branch

### VCS Configuration

  - **Type of VCS:** Git
  - **Fetch URL:** You can get this from Bitbucket when you clone a
    repo. Make sure your id is not in the url.
  - **Default branch:** refs/heads/develop
  - **Branch Specification:** +:\<default\>
  - **Authentication method:** Password
  - **UserName:** teamcity
  - **Password:** \<IOC would have this\>
  - **Clean policy:** Always
  - **Clean files policy:** All untracked files

From the left navigation

1.  click on Trigger
2.  Click the button Add new Trigger
3.  If you are creating a new trigger. Select from the VCS Trigger

**Add to Branch Filter**

\+:\<default\>

  

## Release

### Build configuration - VCS page

Under the Additional Options

  - **VCS checkout mode:**Always checkout files on server
  - **Checkout directory:**Auto (recommended)
  - **Clean Build:** Check Delete all files in the checkout directory
    before the build
  - **default branch settings:** Check Allow builds in the default
    branch

### VCS Configuration

  - **Type of VCS:** Git

  - **Fetch URL:** You can get this from Bitbucket when you clone a
    repo. Make sure your id is not in the url.

  - **Default branch:** refs/heads/master

  - **Branch Specification:**  
    \+:\*
    
    \-:\<default\>
    
    \-:refs/heads/master
    
    \-:refs/heads/develop
    
    \-:refs/heads/feature/\*
    
    \-:refs/heads/hotfix/\*

  - **Authentication method:** Password

  - **UserName:** teamcity

  - **Password:** \<IOC would have this\>

  - **Clean policy:** Always

  - **Clean files policy:** All untracked files

  

From the left navigation

1.  click on Trigger
2.  Click the button Add new Trigger
3.  If you are creating a new trigger. Select from the VCS Trigger
4.    

**Add to Branch Filter**

\+:refs/heads/release/\*

\-:refs/heads/hotfix/\*

\-:\<default\>

\-:refs/heads/master

\-:refs/heads/develop

\-:refs/heads/feature/\*

</div>

<div id="expander-565765405" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-565765405" class="expand-control">

Octopus

</div>

<div id="expander-content-565765405" class="expand-content">

Author: [Ryan Kajiura](https://wiki.pinnacle.com/display/~ryank)

Continuous Delivery (CD) is the process to build, test, configure and
deploy from a build to a production environment. Multiple testing or
staging environments create a *Release Pipeline* to automate the
creation of infrastructure and deployment of a new. Successive
environments support progressively longer-running activities of
integration, load, and user acceptance testing. Continuous Integration
starts the CD process and the pipeline stages each successive
environment the next upon successful completion of tests.

Continuous Delivery may sequence multiple deployment “rings” for
progressive exposure (also known as “controlling the blast radius”).
Progressive exposure groups users who get to try new releases to monitor
their experience in “rings.” The first deployment ring is often a
“canary” used to test new versions in production before a broader
rollout. CD automates deployment from one ring to the next and may
optionally depend on an approval step, in which a decision maker signs
off on the changes electronically. CD may create an auditable record of
the approval in order to satisfy regulatory procedures or other control
objectives.

Without Continuous Delivery, software release cycles were previously a
bottleneck for application and operation teams. Manual processes led to
unreliable releases that produced delays and errors. These teams often
relied on handoffs that resulted in issues during release cycles. The
automated release pipeline allows a “fail fast” approach to validation,
where the tests most likely to fail quickly are run first and
longer-running tests happen after the faster ones complete successfully.

Continuous Delivery is a lean practice. The goal of CD is to keep
production fresh by achieving the shortest path from the availability of
new code in version control or new components in package management to
deployment. By automation, CD minimizes the time to deploy and *time to
mitigate* or *time to remediate* production incidents (TTM and TTR). In
lean terms, this optimizes process time and eliminates idle time.
Continuous Delivery is helped considerably by the complementary
practices of [Infrastructure as
Code](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/devops/learn/what-is-infrastructure-as-code) and
[Monitoring](https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/devops/learn/what-is-monitoring).

Continuous Delivery also supports two other patterns for progressive
exposure beside sequential rings. “Blue/Green deployment” relies on
keeping an existing (blue) version live while a new (green) one is
deployed. Typically, this uses load balancing to direct increasing
amounts of traffic to the green deployment. If monitoring discovers an
incident, traffic can be rerouted to the blue deployment still running.
“Feature flags” (or “feature toggles”) comprise another technique used
for experimentation and “dark launches.” Feature flags turn on features
on or off for different end users based on their identity and group
membership.

  

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Pinnacle Global Configurations**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

<div id="expander-1175577072" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1175577072" class="expand-control">

Lifecycles

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1175577072" class="expand-content">

This part of Octopus refers to the SDLC (Software Development LifeCycle)

Projects are being consolidated to use ITDev - Development and ITDev -
Promotion Path.

### ITDev - Development

![](attachments/446664019/446666054.png)

### ITDev - Promotion Path

![](attachments/446664019/446666055.png)

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1995189011" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1995189011" class="expand-control">

Script Modules

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1995189011" class="expand-content">

Generic and centralize PowerShell scripts that is managed by [Continuous
Deployment & Delivery (Octopus)](446664019.html). Duplication/Clone of
any sort will be removed. Do not make any code modification directly in
Octopus, code will be automatically updated (replace existing)

### Configure IIS - Script Module - All Can use

Generic method to create the IIS structure

### Customer - Install OrleansSiloHost

Install and start Orleans Silo Host server.

Will be renamed to not team specific

### Customer - StopAndDisalePreviousVersion - Script Modules

Generic script to stop previous window service, start current version,
and delete legacy window service.

Will be renamed to not team specific

### DatabaseProjectExecuteSQL

Generic script to manage the order SQL scripts needs to be executed on
target server

### ExecuteReadyAPI - Script Modules - All Can Use

Generic script for Automation testing to execute SoaUI/ReadyAPI projects
after it has been deployed.

### ExecuteSelenium - Script Modules - All Can use

Generic script for Automation testing to execute Selenium projects after
it has been deployed.

### ExecuteSQL - Script Module - All Can Use

Generic method to execute a single SQL file or single SQL query.

### SendEmails - Script Module - All can Use

Generic method that sends emails and attachments. Same code being used
in Team City to send emails out.

### ExecuteWindowsTaskScheduler - Script Module - All Can Use

Generic method that Create/Update Window Task scheduler

### ITDev  - Debug Logs (PowerShell)

Generic function that will output all variables during the build. Will
only be shown in the build logs.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-216618624" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-216618624" class="expand-control">

Variablesets

</div>

<div id="expander-content-216618624" class="expand-content">

Just like Team City Project Hierarchy. There should be a hierarchy
structure as well. Variables can be override as well.

### Global

Generic values All teams should be reference. One already exists Common
Variables - Global Variables. The values at this level should NOT be
duplicated or clone elsewhere.

Example: SMTP Address, port number,

### Team Level

Values that is common for most projects allocated to the team.

Example: Slack channel, slack channel email

One exists for reference ITDev - Global Variables, ITDev - Test
Automation, and Database Administrator.

### Project Level

In theory most there should not be that many variables at this level.
Just overriding Global or Team Level if done correctly.

Example: Any projects under ITDev - Test Automation.

## Debugging

  - All PowerShell scripts should have an optional parameter DebugMode.
    This parameter accepts PowerShell Boolean. This parameter will
    output all parameters name and value that was passed in.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-254643481" class="expand-container">

Step Templates

<div id="expander-control-2003373455" class="expand-control">

ITDev - Deployment Process

</div>

<div id="expander-content-2003373455" class="expand-content">

## Purpose

Centralize process to deploy package to target environment.

### Steps

#### Pre-deployment

1.  Get package from Octopus repository
2.  Stop IIS AppPool
3.  Create/Update IIS configuration

#### Deployment

1.  Deploy package
2.  Output all Octopus variables

#### Post-deployment

1.  Start IIS AppPool
2.  Designate target environment Appsettings.json or Web.config. Remove
    the rest of the files
3.  (.NET Application) - Encrypt web.config file
4.  Create Artifacts

### Template

<http://octopus.pinnacle.com/octopus/app#/library/steptemplates/ActionTemplates-282>

### Source Code

Pre-Deployment:
<https://stash.pinnacle.com/projects/CUS/repos/powershell-scripts/browse/Octopus%20Deployment%20Scripts/ITDev%20Process%20-%201%20PreDeploy.ps1>

Deployment:
<https://stash.pinnacle.com/projects/CUS/repos/powershell-scripts/browse/Octopus%20Deployment%20Scripts/ITDev%20Process%20-%202%20Deploy.ps1>

Post-Deployment:
<https://stash.pinnacle.com/projects/CUS/repos/powershell-scripts/browse/Octopus%20Deployment%20Scripts/ITDev%20Process%20-%203%20PostDeploy.ps1>

      - <https://dbatools.io/>

  

### Installing DBA Tools

#### PowerShell command line.

> This only works in PowerShell version 5+

In PowerShell, run as Administrator. Execute this command Install-Module
-Name dbatools

### Download From Github

In PowerShell, run as Administrator. Execute this command
Invoke-Expression (Invoke-WebRequest -UseBasicParsing
<https://dbatools.io/in>)

copy "C:\\Users\\\<login
User\>\\Documents\\WindowsPowerShell\\Modules\\dbatools" to "C:\\Program
Files\\WindowsPowerShell\\Modules"  

#### Manual

  - [Download the modal
    https://dbatools.io/download/](https://dbatools.io/download/)
  - Update all Environment Paths
      - $env:PSMODULEPATH
      - C:\\Users\\\<User
        Profile\>\\Documents\\WindowsPowerShell\\Modules;
      - C:\\Program Files\\WindowsPowerShell\\Modules
      - C:\\Windows\\system32\\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\Modules\\
      - C:\\Program Files (x86)\\Microsoft SQL
        Server\\130\\Tools\\PowerShell\\Modules\\
      - C:\\Program Files (x86)\\Microsoft SQL
        Server\\120\\Tools\\PowerShell\\Modules\\
