<div id="expander-32177660" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-32177660" class="expand-control">

Role in DevOps

</div>

<div id="expander-content-32177660" class="expand-content">

Author: [Ryan Kajiura](https://wiki.pinnacle.com/display/~ryank)

  

In order to build, test, and release software faster and more reliably.
DevOps introduce some set of practice that automates the processes
between software development and IT teams.

DevOps aimed not only to improve the process of feature releases but
also to reduce defects, so that products can gain high level of quality.
DevOps reduce the process cost related with delivering working product
in incremental approach. DevOps dealing with small, rapid, iterative
development.

The changes that each release having clarity, consistency and
collaboration to understand each other. Changes also been affected in
production environment and customer environment. QA team design details
test plan based on those changes. Operation and development team need to
come on same umbrella. This time specified methodology and tools play a
vital role. Each team following their own designed methodology that best
suit with their skill and process. But goals are common. That is quality
products in a very short time.

![](https://miro.medium.com/max/3483/1*BZUIwLExSu3slCz5mu_ETw.png)

Testers and developers both play important roles in DevOps.

Normally test Process are based on some steps that following all test
levels until product ready for final deployment. Consider those
activities that describe below.

  - a. QA team gets build after it successfully deployed. Here planed
    test environment is the key factor that influence test.
  - b. Then QA team perform test execution based on pre planed test case
    or without defined test cases.
  - c. Test execution may be Manual or Automated.
  - d. Functional and Regression testing are main concern.
  - After QA team meets exit criteria then they stopped testing. Then
    this build finally goes into the production server.

Now think about**DevOps**. In DevOps, test scenario is different from
traditional test process. As quickly as possible QA transfer fresh
development code into the production environment with the collaboration
of the DevOps teams. DevOps engineer then provide the necessary support
on tools and infrastructure to make it a process that works perfectly,
making sure all changes function behaved as expected.

QA team should be focused about quality in software development
life-cycle. Testers be part of technical teams. Testers have to consider
manual functional and non-functional testing, and should focus on their
skills and experiences for apply test automation, and define test
strategies.

Testers always think about requirements that must be meet. Testers be
focused on every change and their effect on developing products. In
order to do this, requirements analysis done by testers. Testers find
out test scope. After successfully analysis, quality attributes be
well-introduce. Some quality characteristic be pre-defined by
organizations or by customers. Requirements need to be specific. QA
teams should involve in the requirements process to help and guide
development teams. QA teams need to start thinking about how they can
utilize their skills to add value as more of their day-to-day work is
automated.

Risk based testing also have large benefits. Testers have to do
regression testing when major changes that may affect other functions as
well. In this scenario automate regression test play very important role
by maximum test coverage.

QA teams should play positive attitude and try most effective
communication way with teams so their technique can add the value by all
possible way in the software development life cycle.

As a tester, the following core tasks need to be maintained through the
life cycle.

  - Engineers and QA activities should be one lined based on standard
    that expected.
  - Try to automate test cases.
  - All deployment must be automated.
  - Test cases that are automated should be perfectly aligned with the
    Continuous Integration cycle.
  - Proper utilization of test automation tools and Continuous
    Integration tools.

From a logistical perspective, Ernest Mueller, lean systems manager for
AlienVault and organizer of DevOps Days Austin says, there are three
likely ways to see QA roles reassigned to better fit DevOps
organizations.

First, there’s the opportunity to embed QA expertise directly within
product teams to directly support them. This is an area that has been
most effective in dealing with QA transition so far, says Steve
Anderson, CEO of the DevOps and agile consultancy Clutch. “The most
successful ways I’ve seen where you still get a hybrid going on is where
a QA is directly embedded into the sprint team or the scrum team, where
they’re involved from the get-go,” he says. “They get the user’s story.
They’re writing test cases.”

Second, Mueller says, there’s also the potential for diverting QA pros
into tooling groups responsible for writing the test harness or
providing tooling across the organization.

And third, there’s the opportunity for creating a center of excellence
or consulting group meant to advise specific work groups on strategic
issues of quality. “That can be tricky, because having the separate
consulting group can easily turn into doing it the way you used to
work,” he explains. “It’s a very subtle approach change that you have
to make. It’s not like they’re not doing work for you. They’re providing
expert consulting so you can do the work better.”

The speed of automation should have QA working within a totally
different paradigm, says Wayne Ariola, chief strategy officer for
Parasoft, a testing and service virtualization firm. “Today we’re mostly
in causal observation mode: Build the test, experience the defect,
collect the defect — it’s causal. Something happened, we collected it,”
he says. “We need to move to a more probabilistic mode.

“This means getting to know the internal application much more as
testers than we do today,” he says. “This also means we have to
understand the dependencies associated with the operational testing.”

The truth is that there is still plenty of room for testing
professionals in the era of DevOps. They just need to adapt to a
rewritten organizational hierarchy — and a completely different mindset
about testing objectives.

For maintain higher accuracy on quality, it is necessary to automate all
testing processes by accurately configuring for auto deployment. QA team
should Keep in their mind that all process should be done without any
failure.

Concentrating on the customer needs, tester give focus on validating
product in short time and gaining high level of quality. A good tester
should not mess with time and quality when more builds are on pipeline.

  

  

  

  

<div id="expander-1936667680" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1936667680" class="expand-control">

</div>

  - [Medium - Role of testers in
    devops](https://medium.com/oceanize-geeks/role-of-testers-in-devops-56e790792cd7)

</div>

</div>

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1903440840" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1903440840" class="expand-control">

Installation & Server Configuration

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1903440840" class="expand-content">

## Environments

### HQ-CI-SEL-01

Windows Edition: Windows Server 2008 R2 Enterprise - SP 1

#### Purpose

Regression Test - Run all test cases on a nightly bases and provide
reports to QA team

  

## Libraries that need to be installed and kept up to date.

#### NodeJS

Latest version of "Current Latest Feature" (Should keep this up to
date).

When upgrading - need to uninstall existing version before install newer
version) or you can run Install\_NodeJS.ps1

#### PowerShell

Current version 5.1 (Should keep this up to date).

  

  

We support multiple programming languages for Selenium.

  - Java
  - Python
  - C\#

### Installation and Configuration:

### HQ-CI-SEL-01

#### Selenium

1.  [Install Selenium 
    https://www.seleniumhq.org](https://www.seleniumhq.org/)
2.  Install Maven <https://maven.apache.org/install.html>
    1.  Install directory "C:\\Program Files\\Apache\\maven"  (Remove
        Version from folder name)
    2.  Add System Variable **M2\_HOME** value **C:\\Program
        Files\\Apache\\maven**
    3.  Add System Variable **MAVEN\_HOME** value **C:\\Program
        Files\\Apache\\maven**
    4.  Add System Variable **Path** value **%M2\_HOME%\\bin;**
3.  Install the supported programming language Chrome Web Driver. 
    [https://www.seleniumhq.org](https://www.seleniumhq.org/)
    1.  Python - C:\\SeleniumWebDrivers\\chromedriverPython
    2.  Java - C:\\SeleniumWebDrivers\\chromedriverJava
    3.  C\#  - C:\\SeleniumWebDrivers\\chromedriverCSharp
4.  Install Java JDK
    <https://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/webnotes/install/windows/jdk-installation-windows.html#Check>
    1.  Add System variables **Java\_Home** value \<installation
        directory\>
    2.  Add System variables **Path** value **%JDK\_HOME%\\bin**
5.  Install latest version of Python
    h<span>ttps://www.python.org/downloads/windows/</span>
    1.  Add System Variable **Path** with Python installation location.
        Example  **C:\\Program Files (x86)\\Python36-32\\Scripts\\;**
6.  Install Octopus tentacle to the server for deployments

#### SoapUI

1.  Install SoapUI / Ready API
2.  Install JRE (if JDK is not installed and/or Selenium is on a
    different server.)

#### Octopus Deployments

Parent folders where created for Selenium and SoapUI projects. They will
be deployed to subfolders

#### Selenium

  - C:\\SeleniumProjects\\Python
  - C:\\SeleniumProjects\\Java
  - C:\\SeleniumProjects\\CSharp

#### SoapUI

  - C:\\SoapProjects

  

  

  

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

Automation Test Server

</div>

<div id="expander-content-422865554" class="expand-content">

## Servers

  - HQ-CI-SEL-01

## Configuration

### Scheduler

We had issues configuring and executing from Windows Task Scheduler. We
moved to Splintware Scheduler tool

  - <https://www.splinterware.com/products/scheduler.html>

Scheduler Configuration

**Event Type:** Run Application

**Event is Enabled:** checked

**Title:** SeleniumProject\_PinnacleWebsite

**Application:**
C:\\Windows\\System32\\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\powershell.exe

**Parameters:** -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy unrestricted
C:\\SeleniumProjects\\ExecuteScripts\\RunSeleniumTest.ps1
-TestProjectDirectory Java\\PinnacleWebsite\\base-workspace
-EmailAddressTo "'clinton.montroos@[pinnacle.com](http://pinnacle.com),
<ryan.kajiura@crescendotechnology.com>'" -TestProjectName AllTest -Suite
PinnacleWebsite -Environment CI

**Schedule Type:***Every Day / Week*

**Daily:***check it all*

**Specific Time:** 05:00

  

## Test Execution

### Selenium

  - Can be executed when deployed through Octopus
  - can be executed by remote on to the server and execute the Window
    Task Scheduler
  - Window task scheduler is configured to run nightly

### SoapUI

## Test Cases

  - Runs all test cases

<div id="expander-392883381" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-392883381" class="expand-control">

Selenium - Coding

</div>

<div id="expander-content-392883381" class="expand-content">

### Testing Framework

Based on the code base Selenium has been written in. We all must use the
same testing frameworks.

<div class="table-wrap">

| Code Base | Testing Framework | References                                                                                     |
| --------- | ----------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| C\#       | MS Test           | <https://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/dd286683.aspx>                                       |
| Java      | TestNG            | h[ttp://testng.org/doc/documentation-main.html](http://testng.org/doc/documentation-main.html) |
| Python    | UnitTest          | Unit Test <https://docs.python.org/3/library/unittest.html>                                    |

</div>

  

### Categories Test Cases

Each code base has different ways to group the test cases. 

Categorizing test cases we can have utilize one project for all the
environment destination as well as reusing same test case for different
environments.

#### Test Categories

1.  FunctionalTest
2.  SmokeTest
3.  SanityCheck
4.  RegressionTest - Do not need to specify this test category.
    Automation Server will execute all test cases ignoring Test Category
    grouping.

All automated test projects will be stored under Team City Test
Automation, under sub project API (SoapUI / ReadyAPI) or UI (Selenium)

Project naming convention format \<Account | Betting | Payment\> -
\<Project Name\> \<API | UI\>

    Examples: 

    Account - Profile API

    Betting - Fatting Lines - UI

Octopus Package naming convention format \*\*/\* =\> \<Account | Betting
| Payments\>.\<Project Name (replace space with period).\<API |
UI\>.%build.number%.zip

    Examples: 

    **/* => Account.Profile.API.%build.number%.zip

    **/* => Betting.Fatting.Lines.API.%build.number%.zip   OR    **/* => Betting.Fatting.Lines.IU.%build.number%.zip

  

All projects must use the build template BuildTemplate - Test Automation

Configure the Configuration Parameter

<div class="table-wrap">

| Parameter Name        | Description                                                                                                          |
| --------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| CodeBase              | (Only for Selenimn) Select the language it was written in. Just need to pick 1 of these \< CSharp | Python | Java \> |
| OctopusChannel        | (no not need to change default) Automation                                                                           |
| OctopusEnvironment    | (no not need to change default) Test Automation Server                                                               |
| OctopusPackagePath    | follow Octopus package naming convention above                                                                       |
| OctopusPackageVersion | (no not need to change default) %build.number%                                                                       |
| OctopusProjectName    | follow project naming convention above.                                                                              |
| OctopusUrl            | obsolete                                                                                                             |

</div>

time if projects take longer.

Octopus Configuration

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1437604614" class="expand-content">

All automated test projects will be stored under Octopus Test Automation
Group

Project Name should match OctopusProjectName

### Process Steps

1.  Deploy Package
    1.  Find and click on <span style="color: rgb(0,128,0);">Configure
        feature</span>
        1.  uncheck everything but
            1.  Custom Installation Directory
            2.  Custom Deployment scripts
    2.  Execution Plan \> Runs on targets in roles test-automation
    3.  Package feed Octopus Server (Built-in)
    4.  Package ID (should match OctopusPackagePath - excluding
        ".%build.number%.zip"
    5.  Custom install directory \> Install to
        "\#{SoapUIPath}\\AccountAccessControlAPI"
        1.  format \#{SoapUIPath}\\\<OctopusProjectName (without
            period)\>
    6.  checked Purge this directory before installation
    7.  Post-deployment script (Everything should be driving from a
        Variable Sets)
    8.  Conditions \> Environment Run for all applicable Lifecycle
        environment
    9.  Conditions \> run condition Always run
2.  Slack - Detailed Notification (Everything should be driving from a
    Variable Sets)  
    1.  Execution Plan Octopus Server
    2.  Webhook URL \#{SlackWebHook} - variable set [Common Variables -
        Global
        Variables](http://octopus.pinnacle.com/octopus/app#/library/variables/LibraryVariableSets-203)
    3.  Channel handle  \#{SlackAutomationChannel} - variable set [Test
        Automation](http://octopus.pinnacle.com/octopus/app#/library/variables/LibraryVariableSets-211)
    4.  Icon URL \#{SlackOctopusIcon} - variable set [Common Variables -
        Global
        Variables](http://octopus.pinnacle.com/octopus/app#/library/variables/LibraryVariableSets-203)
    5.  Username \#{SlackOctupusUserName} - variable set [Common
        Variables - Global
        Variables](http://octopus.pinnacle.com/octopus/app#/library/variables/LibraryVariableSets-203)
    6.  Main message \#{SlackMainMessage}
    7.  check boxes (can have more then what I listed)  
        1.  Include release number field
        2.  include machine name field
        3.  include environment name field
    8.  Octopus base url \#{SlackOctopusBaseURL} - variable set [Common
        Variables - Global
        Variables](http://octopus.pinnacle.com/octopus/app#/library/variables/LibraryVariableSets-203)
    9.  Conditions
        1.  Environment Run for all applicable Lifecycle environment
        2.  run condition Always run
        3.  Start Trigger Wait for the previous step to complete, then
            start

### Script Modules to Include (within the Process tab)

  - ExecuteReadyAPI - Script Module - All Can Use or ExecuteSelenium -
    Script Module - All Can use
  - SendEmails - Script Module - All can use

### Variables

Add these Library Variable Sets

  - Common Variables - Global Variables
  - Customer - Global Variables
  - Test Automation

### Channels

Channel name Automation (Same value as Team City OctopusChannel)

LifeCycle - should be inheriting from project.  Project Lifecycle should
be Test Automation Life Cycle

  

#### Script Modules

There is a generic PowerShell script to execute and send emails to the
designated group when any test case fails. Scripts are maintain and
deployed to Octopus by [Test Automation
Configuration](Test-Automation-Configuration_451824120.html). Everyone
should be using the same generic script - do not create duplicate or
many any changes within Octopus. It will be replace on a regular basis.
Duplication of any sort will be removed.

ExecuteReadyAPI - Script Module - All Can Use is for SoapUI

ExecuteSelenium - Script Module - All Can Use is for Selenium

#### Variable Sets

There is a central library variable call Test Automation. This where all
designated groups will be declared, NOT within the Octopus project
process step.

## Environments

### HQ-CI-SEL-01

Windows Edition: Windows Server 2008 R2 Enterprise - SP 1

#### Purpose

Regression Test - Run all test cases on a nightly bases and provide
reports to QA team

  

## Libraries that need to be installed and kept up to date.

#### NodeJS

Latest version of "Current Latest Feature" (Should keep this up to
date).

When upgrading - need to uninstall existing version before install newer
version) or you can run Install\_NodeJS.ps1

#### PowerShell

Current version 5.1 (Should keep this up to date).

  

  

We support multiple programming languages for Selenium.

  - Java
  - Python
  - C\#

### Installation and Configuration:

### HQ-CI-SEL-01

#### Selenium

1.  [Install Selenium 
    https://www.seleniumhq.org](https://www.seleniumhq.org/)
2.  Install Maven <https://maven.apache.org/install.html>
    1.  Install directory "C:\\Program Files\\Apache\\maven"  (Remove
        Version from folder name)
    2.  Add System Variable **M2\_HOME** value **C:\\Program
        Files\\Apache\\maven**
    3.  Add System Variable **MAVEN\_HOME** value **C:\\Program
        Files\\Apache\\maven**
    4.  Add System Variable **Path** value **%M2\_HOME%\\bin;**
3.  Install the supported programming language Chrome Web Driver. 
    [https://www.seleniumhq.org](https://www.seleniumhq.org/)
    1.  Python - C:\\SeleniumWebDrivers\\chromedriverPython
    2.  Java - C:\\SeleniumWebDrivers\\chromedriverJava
    3.  C\#  - C:\\SeleniumWebDrivers\\chromedriverCSharp
4.  Install Java JDK
    <https://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/webnotes/install/windows/jdk-installation-windows.html#Check>
    1.  Add System variables **Java\_Home** value \<installation
        directory\>
    2.  Add System variables **Path** value **%JDK\_HOME%\\bin**
5.  Install latest version of Python
    h<span>ttps://www.python.org/downloads/windows/</span>
    1.  Add System Variable **Path** with Python installation location.
        Example  **C:\\Program Files (x86)\\Python36-32\\Scripts\\;**
6.  Install Octopus tentacle to the server for deployments

#### SoapUI

1.  Install SoapUI / Ready API
2.  Install JRE (if JDK is not installed and/or Selenium is on a
    different server.)

#### Octopus Deployments

Parent folders where created for Selenium and SoapUI projects. They will
be deployed to subfolders

#### Selenium

  - C:\\SeleniumProjects\\Python
  - C:\\SeleniumProjects\\Java
  - C:\\SeleniumProjects\\CSharp

#### SoapUI

  - C:\\SoapProjects

T-SQL (Transact-SQL)

</div>

<div id="expander-content-195477203" class="expand-content">

<span style="color: rgb(0,0,0);">Author: [Ryan
Kajiura](https://wiki.pinnacle.com/display/~ryank)</span>

  

T-SQL (Transact-SQL) is an extension of SQL language. This tutorial
covers the fundamental concepts of T-SQL such as its various functions,
procedures, indexes, and transactions related to the topic.

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Legend**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

<div id="expander-1833014232" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1833014232" class="expand-control">

Syntax Legend

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1833014232" class="expand-content">

# Transact-SQL Syntax Conventions (Transact-SQL)

<div class="table-wrap">

<table>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th style="text-align: left;">Convention</th>
<th style="text-align: left;">Used for</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td style="text-align: left;">UPPERCASE</td>
<td style="text-align: left;">Transact-SQL keywords.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td style="text-align: left;"><em>italic</em></td>
<td style="text-align: left;">User-supplied parameters of Transact-SQL syntax.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td style="text-align: left;"><strong>bold</strong></td>
<td style="text-align: left;"><div class="content-wrapper">
<p>Type database names, table names, column names, index names, stored procedures, utilities, data type names, and text exactly as shown.</p>
</div></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td style="text-align: left;">underline</td>
<td style="text-align: left;">Indicates the default value applied when the clause that contains the underlined value is omitted from the statement.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td style="text-align: left;">| (vertical bar)</td>
<td style="text-align: left;">Separates syntax items enclosed in brackets or braces. You can use only one of the items.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td style="text-align: left;"><code>[ ]</code>(brackets)</td>
<td style="text-align: left;">Optional syntax items. Don't type the brackets.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td style="text-align: left;">{ } (braces)</td>
<td style="text-align: left;">Required syntax items. Don't type the braces.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td style="text-align: left;">[<strong>,</strong>...<em>n</em>]</td>
<td style="text-align: left;">Indicates the preceding item can be repeated<em>n</em>number of times. The occurrences are separated by commas.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td style="text-align: left;">[...<em>n</em>]</td>
<td style="text-align: left;">Indicates the preceding item can be repeated<em>n</em>number of times. The occurrences are separated by blanks.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td style="text-align: left;">;</td>
<td style="text-align: left;">Transact-SQL statement terminator. Although the semicolon isn't required for most statements in this version of SQL Server, it will be required in a future version.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td style="text-align: left;">&lt;label&gt; ::=</td>
<td style="text-align: left;">The name for a block of syntax. Use this convention to group and label sections of lengthy syntax or a unit of syntax that you can use in more than one location within a statement. Each location in which the block of syntax could be used is indicated with the label enclosed in chevrons: &lt;label&gt;.<br />
<br />
A set is a collection of expressions, for example &lt;grouping set&gt;; and a list is a collection of sets, for example &lt;composite element list&gt;.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</div>

## Multipart Names

Unless specified otherwise, all Transact-SQL references to the name of a
database object can be a four-part name in the following form:

*server\_name*.\[*database\_name*\].\[*schema\_name*\].*object\_name*

|*database\_name*.\[*schema\_name*\].*object\_name*

|*schema\_name*.*object\_name*

|*object\_name*

*server\_name*  
Specifies a linked server name or remote server name.

*database\_name*  
Specifies the name of a SQL Server database when the object resides in a
local instance of SQL Server. When the object is in a linked
server,*database\_name*specifies an OLE DB catalog.

*schema\_name*  
Specifies the name of the schema that contains the object if the object
is in a SQL Server database. When the object is in a linked
server,*schema\_name*specifies an OLE DB schema name.

*object\_name*  
Refers to the name of the object.

When referencing a specific object, you don't always have to specify the
server, database, and schema for the SQL Server Database Engine to
identify the object. However, if the object can't be found, an error is
returned.

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Beginner**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

<div id="expander-49431224" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-49431224" class="expand-control">

SQL & NOSQL

</div>

<div id="expander-content-49431224" class="expand-content">

Author: [Ryan Kajiura](https://wiki.pinnacle.com/display/~ryank)

  

![](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/1-4.png)

  

  

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Relational Database**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

A***relational database***is a set of formally described tables
(*lists*in our example) from which***data***can be accessed or
reassembled in many different ways without having to reorganize
the***database***tables. There are many different types of relational
databases — lined paper, sadly, not being one of them\!

A hallmark feature of the most popular relational databases is a query
language called SQL (Standard Query Language). Meaning that, if Grandma
upgrades her remembering system to a computer, she’d be able to quickly
answer questions like, “Who hasn’t visited me in the last year, is
married, and doesn’t have any hobbies?”

Among the world’s most popular choices for a SQL Database Management
System is MySQL, which is open-source. It is implemented primarily as a
Relational Database Management System (RDBMS) for web-based software
applications.

Some key features of MySQL include:

  - It’s really well known, commonly used, and thoroughly tested.
  - There’s a lot of qualified developers experienced in SQL and
    relational databases.
  - Data gets stored in various tables, allowing easy relations using
    primary and foreign keys (fancy speak for*id*s).
  - It’s easy to use and performant, making it ideal for big and small
    businesses.
  - The source code is under the GNU General Public License agreement.

</div>

</div>

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**No SQL**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

Many **NoSQL **(“not only” SQL)** databases** exist. In our examples, we
exemplified a *Document database. *NoSQL databases model data in ways
that exclude the tabular relations provided in relational databases.
These databases became popular in the early 2000s amongst companies that
required cloud-based database clustering due to their sheer scaling
requirements (i.e. Facebook). In such applications, having data
consistency was a lot less important than performance and scalability.

In the early days, NoSQL databases often got used for super focused data
management tasks. Mainly when it came to web and cloud apps, NoSQL DB’s
have been proven to process and distribute significant volumes of data.
Engineers building with NoSQL have also liked the flexible data schema
(or complete lack thereof), so that fast changes to apps being updated
often were possible.

The key features of NoSQL include:

  - A highly flexible way of persisting data
  - Horizontal scaling to clusters
  - Eventual consistency on persistence/propagation
  - Documents that are identified using unique keys

The huge data set has introduced the challenges of data storage, data
management, data analysis, etc. Moreover, it becomes semi-structured and
sparse. In the case of RDBMS, there is a need for upfront schema and
relational references.

To resolve these problems related to semi-structured or unstructured
data, a range of new database products has emerged during the last few
years. The new class of database products consists of column-based data
stores, key-value pair databases, and document databases, etc. When used
together, these databases are called NoSQL consist of diverse products
each having a unique set of features and propositions.

Other than this, NoSQL databases can be scaled out easily when compared
to SQL databases. The load is distributed among multiple hosts as shown
below whenever load increases.

![](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/2-3.png)

## Features of NoSQL database

### Non-Relational

  - NoSQL databases never follow the relational database models.
  - It never provides a table with fixed column records.
  - It works with self-contained aggregates.
  - It does not require any data normalization or object-relational
    mapping.
  - There are no complex features like relational databases.

### Distributed Computing

  - It is possible to execute multiple databases in a distributed
    manner.
  - It offers fail-over capabilities and auto-scaling features.
  - It can be used with all programming language, or there is no
    standard query to use with NoSQL databases.
  - It provides eventual consistency.
  - It provides no synchronous replication among distributed nodes.
  - It enables maximum distribution and less coordination among data
    nodes.

![Distributed
Computing](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/3-2.png)

### Schema-Free

  - NoSQL databases either have relaxed schemas or it is schema-free.
  - It does not require any definition for the schema of the data.
  - It offers heterogeneous data structures for the same domains.

![Schema-Free](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/4-2.png)

### Simple API

  - It offers easy to use interface for data storage and data query.
  - It allows low-level selection methods and low-level data
    manipulation.
  - It uses text-based protocols with HTTP and JSON.
  - It has no standard-based query language.
  - It is a web-enabled database running as internet-facing services.

## NoSQL Database Types you should know

![NoSQL Database Types you should
know](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/5-2.png)

There are four classes of NoSQL databases with their unique attributes
and limitations. You should understand each of them in depth first and
choose the best one that suits your requirements the most. Let us see
each of them one by one.

### Key-value pair based

This database is designed to manage heavy loads and a lot of data
gracefully. It stores data in key-value pairs where each key is unique
and value can be anything like object, string JSON, etc. Here is one
quick example of the database given below.

![NoSQL Database Types
](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/6-1.png)

It is the most basic type of database that can be used as collections,
arrays, dictionaries, etc. It helps developers to store the schema-less
data. It works best for shopping cart content.

### Column-based NoSQL Database

This database is column-oriented where each column is treated
separately, and values are stored contiguously. Here is the simple
example of how column-based NoSQL database looks like:

![NoSQL Database Types
](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/7-1.png)

It works best for aggregation queries like SUM, Count, MAX, MIN, AVG,
etc. It helps to find data quickly in columns. This database is majorly
used for managing catalogs, data warehouse, BI projects, CRM, or
library, etc.

### Document-Oriented NoSQL Database

It stores and retrieves the data as key-value pair, but the value is
stored in documents in XML or JSON formats. A database itself
understands or queries the data. In the diagram, you can see a table
where data is stored in row and column format. And the right-hand side
is covered by documents where data is stored in JSON format. Here, you
don’t have to define columns which makes it more flexible as compared to
relational databases.

![Document-Oriented NoSQL
Database](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/8-1.png)

It is mostly used for blogging platforms, CRM systems, or real-time
analytics, etc. it is used for complex transactions that require
multiple operations against varying aggregate functions.

## Graph-based NoSQL Databases

![Graph-based NoSQL
Databases](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/9-1.png)

This database stores the entity and defines the relationship among
different entities. The stored entity is named as the node, and the
relationship is defined as the edge. Each node and edge must have a
unique identifier. Here, tables are multi-relational in nature, not
loosely connected. Traversing relationship is much faster in NoSQL
databases when compared to relational databases. It is mostly used for
logistics, networks, and spatial data.

### Query Mechanism tools for NoSQL Database

The data retrieval mechanism in NoSQL database is REST-based  the value
is retrieved based on key/ID with the GET resource. Document stores the
most difficult queries as they use the key-value pair to store the data.
For example, Couch DB define views with the MapReduce.

### What is the CAP Theorem?

This theorem is given by the Brewer which states that it is not possible
for distributed data stores to give more than two out of total three
guarantees. These are consistency, partition tolerance, and
availability.

1). Consistency:

The data should remain consistent even after the execution of an
operation, it means once data is written, any future read request should
be able to access the same data. For example, once you update the status
of an order, the client should be able to check the same data.

2). Partition Tolerance:

If communication among servers is not stable even then the system should
be able to work properly, it is called the partition tolerance. For
example, when the server is divided into multiple partitions, they may
or may not communicate together. If one part of the database is
unavailable even then other parts should not be affected.

3). Availability:

The database should be highly responsive and available without any
downtime.

### Eventual Consistency

The term eventual consistency means multiple data copies are available
on different machines to get higher availability and scalability. If
some changes are made to one file, it should automatically be reflected
other replicas.

Data replication is not instantaneous because a few copies are updated
frequently and a few over time. But you have to make sure content is the
same for all replicas. Hence, the name of this phenomenon is given as
eventual consistency.

BASE: Basically Available, Soft state, Eventual consistency

![Graph-based NoSQL
Databases](https://www.janbasktraining.com/blog/uploads/images/2019/04/10-1.png)

  - Here basically available means DB is available all the time as per
    the assumption of CAP theorem.
  - Soft state means the state of a system may change without an input.
  - Eventual consistency means system become consistent over time.

### Advantages of NoSQL Database

The desired technical characteristics for NoSQL database are given as
below.

#### Primary and Analytic Data Source Capability

The first criteria for any NoSQL solution are that it must serve as the
primary or active data source that receives data from different business
apps. It should act as the secondary data source or analytical database
to enhance the overall functionalities of business apps. Further, it
should be capable of integrating with different types of data like
structured, semi-structured, or unstructured. Additionally, it can
execute complex queries too.

#### Big Data Capability

NoSQL databases are good with Big data, and they can be scaled quickly
to manage voluminous data from terabytes to petabytes. Additionally, it
delivers high performance for data velocity, data complexity, and the
data variety.

#### Continuous Availability

NoSQL database is always available without any single point of failure.
All nodes in the cluster can read request even if some machine is down.
It can replicate data among different physical machines within a data
center. It avoids hardware outages too.

#### Multi-Data Center Capability

Business enterprises need highly distributed databases that are spread
across multiple data centers or graphical locales without any
performance issues. The solution includes the ability to handle multiple
data centers without concerning the overall occurrences of read and
write operations. A good NoSQL database supports multiple data centers
and provides configuration options to maintain a proper balance between
consistency and performance.

#### Separate Cache layer is not required

A good NoSQL database uses and distributes data among different
participating nodes. It does not have a separate cache layer to store
the data. The memory cache of multiple participating nodes stores data
quickly for immediate I/O access. It eliminates the problems of
synchronizing cache data with the persistent database. In this way, it
supports higher scalability with fewer management issues.

#### Cloud-Ready

The adoption of cloud platforms is increasing daily by leading
enterprises worldwide. This is the reason why every robust platform must
be cloud-ready. NoSQL databases like MongoDB are cloud-ready able to
work in a cloud setting when necessary. It supports the hybrid solution
when one part of the database is hosted within the enterprise, and
another part is hosted in the cloud.

#### High Performance and Scalability

NoSQL databases can enhance performance by adding multiple nodes to the
cluster. Usually, the performance of a database system goes down with
additional nodes to a cluster. However, a good NoSQL database increases
performance for both read and write operations when new nodes are added,
and performance gains are linear in nature.

Here, we have listed the major benefits of the NoSQL database but there
a few more as discussed by enterprises like easy to implement, easy to
use, supports multiple languages & platforms, thriven open source
community, etc.

  

</div>

</div>

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**SQL vs NoSQL**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

![](attachments/451823902/463527378.jpg)

  

<div class="table-wrap">

<table>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th style="text-align: left;">RDBMS</th>
<th style="text-align: left;">NOSQL</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td style="text-align: left;"><ul>
<li>Data is stored in a relational model, with rows and columns.</li>
<li>A row contains information about an item while columns contain specific information, such as 'Model', 'Date of Manufacture', 'Color'.</li>
<li>Follows fixed schema. Meaning, the columns are defined and locked before data entry. In addition, each row contains data for each column.</li>
<li>Supports vertical scaling. Scaling an RDBMS across multiple servers is a challenging and time-consuming process</li>
<li>Atomicity, Consistency, Isolation &amp; Durability(ACID) Compliant</li>
</ul></td>
<td style="text-align: left;"><ul>
<li>Data is stored in a host of different databases, with different data storage models.</li>
<li>Follows dynamic schemas. Meaning, you can add columns anytime</li>
<li>Supports horizontal scaling. You can scale across multiple servers. Multiple servers are cheap commodity hardware or cloud instances, which make scaling cost-effective compared to vertical scaling</li>
<li>Not ACID Compliant</li>
</ul></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</div>

</div>

</div>

DataTypes

</div>

<div id="expander-content-484452533" class="expand-content">

## Binary

<div class="table-wrap">

| DataType       | Description                                                                                               |
| -------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| binary         | Fixed-length binary data with a maximum length of 8,000 bytes.                                            |
| varbinary      | Variable-length binary data with a maximum length of 8,000 bytes.                                         |
| varbinary(max) | Variable-length binary data with a maximum length of 2<sup>31</sup>bytes (Introduced in SQL Server 2005). |
| image          | Variable-length binary data with a maximum length of 2,147,483,647 bytes.                                 |

</div>

## Character Strings

<div class="table-wrap">

| DataType     | Description                                                                                               |
| ------------ | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| char         | Fixed-length non-Unicode character data with a maximum length of 8,000 characters.                        |
| varchar      | Variable-length non-Unicode data with a maximum of 8,000 characters.                                      |
| varchar(max) | Variable-length non-Unicode data with a maximum length of 231 characters (Introduced in SQL Server 2005). |
| text         | Variable-length non-Unicode data with a maximum length of 2,147,483,647 characters                        |

</div>

## Unicode Characters

<div class="table-wrap">

| DataType      | Description                                                                                                     |
| ------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| nchar         | Fixed-length Unicode data with a maximum length of 4,000 characters.                                            |
| nvarchar      | Variable-length Unicode data with a maximum length of 4,000 characters.                                         |
| Nvarchar(max) | Variable-length Unicode data with a maximum length of 2<sup>30</sup>characters (Introduced in SQL Server 2005). |
| ntext         | Variable-length Unicode data with a maximum length of 1,073,741,823 characters.                                 |

</div>

## Data and Time

<div class="table-wrap">

| DataType       | Description                                                                                       |
| -------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| datetime       | Jan 1, 1753 to Dec 31, 9999(3.33 milliseconds accuracy)                                           |
| smalldatetime  | Jan 1, 1900 to Jun 6, 2079 (1 minute accuracy)                                                    |
| datetimeoffset | Jan 1, 0001 to Dec 31, 9999 (100 nanoseconds accuracy. Introduced in SQL Server 2008)             |
| datetime2      | Jan 1, 0001 to Dec 31, 9999 (100 nanoseconds accuracy. Introduced in**SQL Server 2008**)          |
| time           | 00:00:00.0000000 to 23:59:59.9999999 (100 nanoseconds accuracy. Introduced in**SQL Server 2008**) |

</div>

## Other Data Types

  - **sql\_variant**− Stores values of various SQL Server-supported data
    types, except text, ntext, and timestamp.

  - **timestamp**− Stores a database-wide unique number that gets
    updated every time a row gets updated.

  - **uniqueidentifier**− Stores a globally unique identifier (GUID).

  - **xml**− Stores XML data. You can store XML instances in a column or
    a variable (Introduced in SQL Server 2005).

  - **cursor**− A reference to a cursor.

  - **table**− Stores a result set for later processing.

  - **hierarchyid**− A variable length, system data type used to
    represent position in a hierarchy (Introduced in SQL Server 2008).

<div id="expander-2023530395" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-2023530395" class="expand-control">

Query Statements

</div>

<div id="expander-content-2023530395" class="expand-content">

<div id="expander-1681575411" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1681575411" class="expand-control">

SELECT Clause

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1681575411" class="expand-content">

SQL Server**SELECT**statement is used to fetch the data from a database
table which returns data in the form of result table. These result
tables are called**result-sets**.Retrieves rows from the database and
enables the selection of one or many rows or columns from one or many
tables in SQL Server

## Syntax

Following is the basic syntax of SELECT statement. Where, column1,
column2...are the fields of a table whose values you want to fetch.

> SELECT column1, column2, columnN FROM table\_name;

  

> \<SELECT statement\> ::=    
> 
>     \[ WITH { \[ XMLNAMESPACES ,\] \[ \<common\_table\_expression\>
> \[,...n\] \] } \]  
> 
>     \<query\_expression\>   
> 
>     \[ ORDER BY { order\_by\_expression | column\_position \[ ASC |
> DESC \] }   
> 
>   \[ ,...n \] \]   
> 
>     \[ \<FOR Clause\>\]   
> 
>     \[ OPTION ( \<query\_hint\> \[ ,...n \] ) \]   
> 
> \<query\_expression\> ::=   
> 
>     { \<query\_specification\> | ( \<query\_expression\> ) }   
> 
>     \[  { UNION \[ ALL \] | EXCEPT | INTERSECT }  
> 
>         \<query\_specification\> | ( \<query\_expression\> ) \[...n \]
> \]   
> 
> \<query\_specification\> ::=   
> 
> SELECT \[ ALL | DISTINCT \]   
> 
>     \[TOP ( expression ) \[PERCENT\] \[ WITH TIES \] \]   
> 
>     \< select\_list \>   
> 
>     \[ INTO new\_table \]   
> 
>     \[ FROM { \<table\_source\> } \[ ,...n \] \]   
> 
>     \[ WHERE \<search\_condition\> \]   
> 
>     \[ \<GROUP BY\> \]   
> 
>     \[ HAVING \< search\_condition \> \]  

## Example

> /\* choose all data in the tbCustomer table \*/
> 
> SELECT \* FROM tbCustomer

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1254735830" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1254735830" class="expand-control">

UPDATE Clause

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1254735830" class="expand-content">

## Syntax

> ## Example
> 
> /\* Update, Change data in table \*/
> 
> UPDATE Customer SET FirstName = 'Arnold' Where CustomerID = 'ts920384'

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1912987632" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1912987632" class="expand-control">

DELETE Clause

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1912987632" class="expand-content">

## Syntax

> ## Example
> 
> /\* Delete data in table \*/
> 
> DELETE FROM customers WHERE CustomerID = 'js001'

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-152393142" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-152393142" class="expand-control">

INSERT Clause

</div>

<div id="expander-content-152393142" class="expand-content">

## Syntax

> ## Example
> 
> /\* Insert data in table \*/
> 
> INSERT INTO tbCustomer (CustomerId, FirstName, LastName, Email, Age)
> 
> VALUES ('JS001',
> 'Pamela','Gravenhorst',pamela@[mail.com](http://mail.com)',40);

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1660484742" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1660484742" class="expand-control">

WHERE Clause

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1660484742" class="expand-content">

The MS SQL Server **WHERE** clause is used to specify a condition while
fetching the data from single table or joining with multiple tables. If
the given condition is satisfied, only then it returns a specific value
from the table. You will have to use WHERE clause to filter the records
and fetch only necessary records.

Specifies the search condition for the rows returned by the query.

Following is the basic syntax of SELECT statement with WHERE clause

## Synatx  

  

> SELECT column1, column2, columnN  
> 
> FROM table\_name
> 
> WHERE \[condition\]

  

> \[ WHERE \<search\_condition\> \]

## Example  

  

> /\* Search specific customer by using specific value \*/
> 
> SELECT \* FROM tbCustomer WHERE customerid = 'SL805093'
> 
> /\* Search data by combining values \*/
> 
> SELECT top 10 \* FROM tbCustomer WHERE Country = 'Germany' AND City =
> 'Berlin'

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1352817951" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1352817951" class="expand-control">

GROUP BY Clause

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1352817951" class="expand-content">

The SQL Server GROUP BY clause is used in collaboration with the SELECT
statement to arrange identical data into groups. The GROUP BY clause
follows the WHERE clause in a SELECT statement and precedes the ORDER BY
clause. A SELECT statement clause that divides the query result into
groups of rows, usually for the purpose of performing one or more
aggregations on each group. The SELECT statement returns one row per
group.Following is the basic syntax of GROUP BY clause. The GROUP BY
clause must follow the conditions in the WHERE clause and must precede
the ORDER BY clause if one is used.

## Syntax

> SELECT column1, column2
> 
> FROM table\_name
> 
> WHERE \[ conditions \]
> 
> GROUP BY column1, column2
> 
> ORDER BY column1, column2

  

> \-- Syntax for SQL Server and Azure SQL Database   
> 
> \-- ISO-Compliant Syntax  
> 
> GROUP BY {
> 
>       column-expression  
> 
>     | ROLLUP ( \<group\_by\_expression\> \[ ,...n \] )  
> 
>     | CUBE ( \<group\_by\_expression\> \[ ,...n \] )  
> 
>     | GROUPING SETS ( \<grouping\_set\> \[ ,...n \]  )  
> 
>     | () --calculates the grand total
> 
> } \[ ,...n \]
> 
> \<group\_by\_expression\> ::=  
> 
>       column-expression  
> 
>     | ( column-expression \[ ,...n \] )    
> 
> \<grouping\_set\> ::=  
> 
>       () --calculates the grand total  
> 
>     | \<grouping\_set\_item\>  
> 
>     | ( \<grouping\_set\_item\> \[ ,...n \] )  
> 
> \<grouping\_set\_item\> ::=  
> 
>       \<group\_by\_expression\>  
> 
>     | ROLLUP ( \<group\_by\_expression\> \[ ,...n \] )  
> 
>     | CUBE ( \<group\_by\_expression\> \[ ,...n \] )  
> 
> \-- For backward compatibility only.
> 
> \-- Non-ISO-Compliant Syntax for SQL Server and Azure SQL Database
> 
> GROUP BY
> 
>       \[ ALL \] column-expression \[ ,...n \]

## Example

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-452572809" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-452572809" class="expand-control">

HAVING Clause

</div>

<div id="expander-content-452572809" class="expand-content">

Specifies a search condition for a group or an aggregate. HAVING can be
used only with the SELECT statement. HAVING is typically used with a
GROUP BY clause. When GROUP BY is not used, there is an implicit single,
aggregated group.

## Syntax  

> \[ HAVING \<search condition\> \]

## Example

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-448252631" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-448252631" class="expand-control">

ORDER BY Clause

</div>

<div id="expander-content-448252631" class="expand-content">

The MS SQL Server **ORDER** BY clause is used to sort the data in
ascending or descending order, based on one or more columns. Some
database sort query results in ascending order by default.

Following is the basic syntax of ORDER BY clause.

## Syntax

> SELECT column-list  
> 
> FROM table\_name  
> 
> \[WHERE condition\]  
> 
> \[ORDER BY column1, column2, .. columnN\] \[ASC | DESC\];

  

> \-- Syntax for SQL Server and Azure SQL Database  
> 
> ORDER BY order\_by\_expression  
> 
>     \[ COLLATE collation\_name \]   
> 
>     \[ ASC | DESC \]   
> 
>     \[ ,...n \]   
> 
> \[ \<offset\_fetch\> \]  
> 
> \<offset\_fetch\> ::=  
> 
> {   
> 
>     OFFSET { integer\_constant | offset\_row\_count\_expression } {
> ROW | ROWS }  
> 
>     \[  
> 
>       FETCH { FIRST | NEXT } {integer\_constant |
> fetch\_row\_count\_expression } { ROW | ROWS } ONLY  
> 
>     \]  

> }

## Example

> /\* choose all data in table and sort by Descending or Ascending \*/
> 
> SELECT \* FROM tbCustomer ORDER BY OpenDateTime DESC
> 
> Or
> 
> SELECT \* FROM tbCustomer ORDER BY OpenDateTime ASC

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1423915769" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1423915769" class="expand-control">

MATCH Clause

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1423915769" class="expand-content">

Specifies a search condition for a graph. MATCH can be used only with
graph node and edge tables, in the SELECT statement as part of WHERE
clause.

## Syntax  

> MATCH (\<graph\_search\_pattern\>)
> 
> \<graph\_search\_pattern\>::=
> 
>   {  
> 
>       \<simple\_match\_pattern\>
> 
>     | \<arbitrary\_length\_match\_pattern\>  
> 
>     | \<arbitrary\_length\_match\_last\_node\_predicate\>
> 
>   }
> 
> \<simple\_match\_pattern\>::=
> 
>   {
> 
>       LAST\_NODE(\<node\_alias\>) | \<node\_alias\>   {
> 
>           { \<-( \<edge\_alias\> )- }
> 
>         | { -( \<edge\_alias\> )-\> }
> 
>         \<node\_alias\> | LAST(\<node\_alias\>)
> 
>         }
> 
>   }
> 
>   \[ { AND } { ( \<simple\_match\_pattern\> ) } \]
> 
>   \[ ,...n \]
> 
> \<node\_alias\> ::=
> 
>   node\_table\_name | node\_table\_alias
> 
> \<edge\_alias\> ::=
> 
>   edge\_table\_name | edge\_table\_alias
> 
> \<arbitrary\_length\_match\_pattern\>  ::=
> 
>   {
> 
>     SHORTEST\_PATH(
> 
>       \<arbitrary\_length\_pattern\>
> 
>       \[ { AND } { \<arbitrary\_length\_pattern\> } \]
> 
>       \[ ,…n\]
> 
>     )
> 
>   }
> 
> \<arbitrary\_length\_match\_last\_node\_predicate\> ::=
> 
>   {  LAST\_NODE( \<node\_alias\> ) = LAST\_NODE( \<node\_alias\> ) }
> 
> \<arbitrary\_length\_pattern\> ::=
> 
>     {  LAST\_NODE( \<node\_alias\> )   | \<node\_alias\>
> 
>      ( \<edge\_first\_al\_pattern\>
> \[\<edge\_first\_al\_pattern\>…,n\] )
> 
>      \<al\_pattern\_quantifier\>
> 
>   }
> 
>      |  ( {\<node\_first\_al\_pattern\> \[\<node\_first\_al\_pattern\>
> …,n\] )
> 
>             \<al\_pattern\_quantifier\>
> 
>         LAST\_NODE( \<node\_alias\> ) | \<node\_alias\>
> 
>  }   
> 
> \<edge\_first\_al\_pattern\> ::=
> 
>   { (  
> 
>         { -( \<edge\_alias\> )-\>   }
> 
>       | { \<-( \<edge\_alias\> )- }
> 
>       \<node\_alias\>
> 
>       )
> 
>   }
> 
> \<node\_first\_al\_pattern\> ::=
> 
>   { (
> 
>       \<node\_alias\>
> 
>         { \<-( \<edge\_alias\> )- }
> 
>       | { -( \<edge\_alias\> )-\> }
> 
>        )
> 
>   }
> 
> \<al\_pattern\_quantifier\> ::=
> 
>   {
> 
>         +
> 
>       | { 1 , n }
> 
>   }
> 
> n -  positive integer only.

  

## Example

  

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-control-1728241608" class="expand-control">

<div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

<div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">

**Intermediate**

</div>

<div class="panelContent">

<div id="expander-1045101734" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1045101734" class="expand-control">

Variables

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1045101734" class="expand-content">

A Transact-SQL local variable is an database object that can store a
single data value of a specific type.

To declare a variable uses the keyword DECLARE, assign a variable name
and a data type.

> DECLARE @MyVariable datatype;

After a variable is declared, it gets the default NULL value. To assign
a value to a variable, use the SET statement.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-569657870" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-569657870" class="expand-control">

Table Joins

</div>

<div id="expander-content-569657870" class="expand-content">

Author: [Ryan Kajiura](https://wiki.pinnacle.com/display/~ryank)

By using joins, you can retrieve data from two or more tables based on
logical relationships between the tables. Joins indicate how SQL Server
should use data from one table to select the rows in another table.

A join condition defines the way two tables are related in a query by:

  - Specifying the column from each table to be used for the join. A
    typical join condition specifies a foreign key from one table and
    its associated key in the other table.
  - Specifying a logical operator (for example, = or \<\>,) to be used
    in comparing values from the columns.

[![](rest/documentConversion/latest/conversion/thumbnail/463531478/1)](/download/attachments/463531476/Types%20of%20SQL%20Join.pdf?version=1&modificationDate=1584363175563&api=v2)

  

<div id="expander-21922350" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-21922350" class="expand-control">

Inner Join

</div>

<div id="expander-content-21922350" class="expand-content">

Returns rows when there is a match in both tables.  Inner joins can be
specified in either the`FROM`or`WHERE`clauses. Outer joins can be
specified in the`FROM`clause only. The join conditions combine with
the`WHERE`and`HAVING`search conditions to control the rows that are
selected from the base tables referenced in the`FROM`clause.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-347386955" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-347386955" class="expand-control">

Left Join

</div>

<div id="expander-content-347386955" class="expand-content">

Returns all rows from the left table, even if there are no matches in
the right table.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-2117046521" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-2117046521" class="expand-control">

Right Join

</div>

<div id="expander-content-2117046521" class="expand-content">

Returns all rows from the right table, even if there are no matches in
the left table.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-2031711701" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-2031711701" class="expand-control">

Full Join

</div>

<div id="expander-content-2031711701" class="expand-content">

Returns rows when there is a match in one of the tables.

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1009525486" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1009525486" class="expand-control">

Self Join

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1009525486" class="expand-content">

This is used to join a table to itself as if the table were two tables,
temporarily renaming at least one table in the MS SQL Server statement.

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1876759552" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1876759552" class="expand-control">

Subquery

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1876759552" class="expand-content">

A SQL Subquery(also called an inner query or inner select) is a sql
query that is nested inside a statement(SELECT, INSERT, UPDATE, or
DELETE), or inside another subquery.

<div id="expander-1775392354" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1775392354" class="expand-control">

IN

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1775392354" class="expand-content">

  

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-control-1783285475" class="expand-control">

</div>

<div id="expander-887067241" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-887067241" class="expand-control">

Arithmetic Operators

</div>

<div id="expander-content-887067241" class="expand-content">

<div class="table-wrap">

|    |          |
| -- | -------- |
| \+ | Add      |
| \- | Subtract |
| \* | Multiply |
| /  | Divide   |
| %  | Modulo   |

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-192857060" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-192857060" class="expand-control">

Bitwise Operators

</div>

<div id="expander-content-192857060" class="expand-content">

<div class="table-wrap">

|   |                      |
| - | -------------------- |
| & | Bitwise AND          |
| | | Bitwise OR           |
| ^ | Bitwise exclusive OR |

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-256671032" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-256671032" class="expand-control">

Comparison Operators

</div>

<div id="expander-content-256671032" class="expand-content">

<div class="table-wrap">

|      |                          |
| ---- | ------------------------ |
| \=   | Equal to                 |
| \>   | Greater than             |
| \<   | Less than                |
| \>=  | Greater than or equal to |
| \<=  | Less than or equal to    |
| \<\> | Not equal to             |

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1560345988" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1560345988" class="expand-control">

Compound Operators

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1560345988" class="expand-content">

<div class="table-wrap">

|      |                          |
| ---- | ------------------------ |
| \+=  | Add Equals               |
| \-=  | Subtract Equals          |
| \*=  | Multiply Equals          |
| /=   | Divide Equals            |
| %=   | Modulo Equals            |
| &=   | Bitwise AND Equals       |
| ^-=  | Bitwise Exclusive Equals |
| |\*= | Bitwise OR Equals        |

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div id="expander-1944334875" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-1944334875" class="expand-control">

Logical Operators

</div>

<div id="expander-content-1944334875" class="expand-content">

<div class="table-wrap">

|         |                                                               |
| ------- | ------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ALL     | TRUE if all of a set of comparisons are TRUE.                 |
| AND     | TRUE if both expressions are TRUE.                            |
| ANY     | TRUE if any one of a set of comparisons are TRUE.             |
| BETWEEN | TRUE if the operand is within the range of comparisons.       |
| EXISTS  | TRUE if a subquery contains any rows.                         |
| IN      | TRUE if the operand is equal to one of a list of expressions. |
| LIKE    | TRUE if the operand matches a pattern.                        |
| NOT     | Reverses the value of any other operator.                     |
| OR      | TRUE if either expression is TRUE.                            |
| SOME    | TRUE if some of a set of comparisons are TRUE.                |

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

</div>

Companies worldwide are using Python to harvest insights from their data and get a competitive edge. Unlike any other Python tutorial, this course focuses on Python specifically for data science. In our Intro to Python class, you will learn about powerful ways to store and manipulate data as well as cool data science tools to start your own analyses. | <https://www.datacamp.com/courses/intro-to-python-for-data-science>        |
| Code like a Pythonista    | In this interactive tutorial, we'll cover many essential Python idioms and techniques in depth, adding immediately useful tools to your belt.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | <http://python.net/~goodger/projects/pycon/2007/idiomatic/handout.html>    |

## Tutorials

<https://www.guru99.com/selenium-tutorial.html>

[http://executeautomation.com/blog/functional-tools/selenium-automation-with-c](http://executeautomation.com/blog/functional-tools/selenium-automation-with-c/)

  

  
  

## Getting Started Summary

\- Selenium - It is used for Web Browser Automation

\- Appium - Mobile testing, Selenium is prerequisite to learn Appium

\- Install JDK

\- Install Eclipse LUNA (For Java Coding)

           - File \>\> New Java project (JRE System Library)

\- Every Java file has its class file, which is platform and OS
independent

\- Group of Classes bundled is called JAR file. JAR file is a collection
of many Class Files (it is also called a Package)

\- Selenium has its own JAR files (inbuilt)

\- Need to add Selenium JAR files in the eclipse, in order to use
inbuilt classes

      --\>
<http://selenium-release.storage.googleapis.com/index.html?path=2.53/>

      -- Download - selenium-java-2.53.0.zip

      -- Unzip

      -- Under Eclipse, Add it by right click on Project \>\> Properties
\>\> Java Build Path \>\> Libraries \>\>  Add External JARs

      -- Add Main Selenium JAR and JARs under Lib to see imported JARs,
under 'Refrenced Libraries' section

\- OOP (Object Oriented Programming)

   - Main function is including only in those classes, which we want to
execute (Public Static Void Main PSVM)

   - An object is an instance of a class and we can create as many
instances (Objects) of a class as required. Objects are created in the
memory

   - Every object needs to have an object reference. Object is a memory
and object reference is a reference or point to that memory e.g. Pen p1
= new Pen();. Here p1 is reference and Pen() is a memory.

  

  

## Selenium Tips & Tricks

<div class="table-wrap">

<table style="width:100%;">
<colgroup>
<col style="width: 6%" />
<col style="width: 32%" />
<col style="width: 38%" />
<col style="width: 22%" />
</colgroup>
<thead>
<tr class="header">
<th>Subject</th>
<th>Description</th>
<th>Example</th>
<th>More info Link</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Implicit Wait</td>
<td>Selenium WebDriver has borrowed the idea of implicit waits from Watir. This means that we can tell Selenium that we would like it to wait for a certain amount of time before throwing an exception that it cannot find the element on the page. We should note that implicit waits will be in place for the entire time the browser is open. This means that any search for elements on the page could take the time the implicit wait is set for.</td>
<td><div class="content-wrapper">
<div class="code panel pdl" style="border-width: 1px;">
<div class="codeContent panelContent pdl">
<pre class="syntaxhighlighter-pre" data-syntaxhighlighter-params="brush: java; gutter: false; theme: Confluence" data-theme="Confluence"><code>Java
WebDriver driver = new FirefoxDriver();
driver.manage().timeouts().implicitlyWait(10, TimeUnit.SECONDS);
driver.get(&quot;http://url_that_delays_loading&quot;);
WebElement myDynamicElement = driver.findElement(By.id(&quot;myDynamicElement&quot;));
 WebDriver driver = new FirefoxDriver();
 
 driver.manage().timeouts().implicitlyWait(10, TimeUnit.SECONDS);
 
 driver.get(&quot;http://url_that_delays_loading&quot;);
 
 WebElement myDynamicElement = driver.findElement(By.id(&quot;myDynamicElement&quot;));</code></pre>
</div>
</div>
</div></td>
<td><br />
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>Explicit Wait</td>
<td>It is more extendible in the means that you can set it up to wait for any condition you might like. Usually, you can use some of the prebuilt ExpectedConditions to wait for elements to become clickable, visible, invisible, etc.</td>
<td><div class="content-wrapper">
<div class="code panel pdl" style="border-width: 1px;">
<div class="codeContent panelContent pdl">
<pre class="syntaxhighlighter-pre" data-syntaxhighlighter-params="brush: java; gutter: false; theme: Confluence" data-theme="Confluence"><code>WebDriverWait wait = new WebDriverWait(driver, 10);
 
WebElement element = wait.until(ExpectedConditions.elementToBeClickable(By.id(&quot;someid&quot;)));</code></pre>
</div>
</div>
</div></td>
<td><br />
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td>Fluent Wait</td>
<td>Each FluentWait instance defines the maximum amount of time to wait for a condition, as well as the frequency with which to check the condition. Furthermore, the user may configure the wait to ignore specific types of exceptions whilst waiting, such as NoSuchElementExceptions when searching for an element on the page.</td>
<td><div class="content-wrapper">
<div class="code panel pdl" style="border-width: 1px;">
<div class="codeContent panelContent pdl">
<pre class="syntaxhighlighter-pre" data-syntaxhighlighter-params="brush: java; gutter: false; theme: Confluence" data-theme="Confluence"><code>// Waiting 30 seconds for an element to be present on the page, checking
 // for its presence once every 5 seconds.
 Wait wait = new FluentWait(driver)
 .withTimeout(30, SECONDS)
 .pollingEvery(5, SECONDS)
 .ignoring(NoSuchElementException.class);
 WebElement foo = wait.until(new Function() {
 public WebElement apply(WebDriver driver) {
 return driver.findElement(By.id(&quot;foo&quot;));
 }
 });</code></pre>
</div>
</div>
</div></td>
<td><br />
</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td>TestNG</td>
<td><p><em>TestNG</em>is a testing framework inspired from <em>JUnit</em>and <em>NUnit</em>but introducing some new functionality that make it more powerful and easier to use.</p>
<p>It is an open source automated testing framework; where <em>NG of TestNG means Next Generation</em>. TestNG is similar to JUnit but it is much more powerful than JUnit but still it’s inspired by JUnit. It is designed to be better than JUnit, especially when testing integrated classes. Pay special thanks to <em>Cedric Beust who is the creator of TestNG</em>.</p>
<p>TestNG eliminates most of the limitations of the older framework and gives the developer the ability to write more flexible and powerful tests with help of easy annotations, grouping, sequencing &amp; parametrizing.</p>
<p><br />
</p></td>
<td><div class="content-wrapper">
<div class="code panel pdl" style="border-width: 1px;">
<div class="codeContent panelContent pdl">
<pre class="syntaxhighlighter-pre" data-syntaxhighlighter-params="brush: java; gutter: false; theme: Confluence" data-theme="Confluence"><code>@Test(description=&quot;Launches the WordPress site&quot;)
public void launchSite(){
 selenium.open(&quot;&quot;);
 selenium.waitForPageToLoad(&quot;30000&quot;);
 assertEquals(selenium.getTitle(), &quot;Demo | Just another WordPress site&quot;);
}</code></pre>
</div>
</div>
<p><br />
</p>
<p><br />
</p>
<p><br />
</p>
</div></td>
<td><a href="http://toolsqa.com/selenium-webdriver/testng-introduction/" class="external-link">http://toolsqa.com/selenium-webdriver/testng-introduction/</a></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</div>

**  
**

  

</div>

SoapUI / Ready API

</div>

<div id="expander-content-100982620" class="expand-content">

  

<div class="confluence-information-macro confluence-information-macro-information">

<span class="aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-info confluence-information-macro-icon"></span>

<div class="confluence-information-macro-body">

SoapUI allows testers to execute automated functional, regression,
compliance, and load tests on different Web API. But SoapUI is not just
a functional API Testing tool, it also let's us perform non-functional
testing such as performance and security tests.

</div>

</div>

<td><div class="content-wrapper">
<div id="expander-1183304186" class="expand-container">
<div id="expander-control-1183304186" class="expand-control">
From Bet Acceptance Team: SoapUI - Automated test cases naming convention
</div>
<div id="expander-content-1183304186" class="expand-content">
<div>
1. <em>TestSuite</em> naming convention: [API operation name] or  [API operation name].[Feature Name]
</div>
<div>
  Examples: PlaceStraightBet, PlaceStraightBet.Automove,  PlaceStraightBet.B2B
</div>
<div>
<img src="attachments/377494204/392400006.png" class="confluence-embedded-image confluence-thumbnail" height="250" />
</div>
<div>
2. All the names of <em><strong>positive</strong> test cases</em> should follow the bellow naming convention:
</div>
<div>
    [testCase #] [short desc][-importantParameter1][-importantParameter2]
</div>
<div>
3. All the names of <em><strong>error handling</strong> test cases</em> should follow the bellow naming convention:
</div>
<div>
    [Error Handling]- [short desc][-ERROR CODE][-importantParameter1][-importantParameter2]
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</div>

  

  

  

</div>

<div id="expander-290135132" class="expand-container">

<div id="expander-control-290135132" class="expand-control">

BlazeMeter & JMeter

</div>

<div id="expander-content-290135132" class="expand-content">

  

<div class="confluence-information-macro has-no-icon confluence-information-macro-information">

<div class="confluence-information-macro-body">

![(info)](images/icons/emoticons/information.svg) This document was
created by Parminderjeet S Bhullar.

</div>

</div>

  

<div class="table-wrap">

<table>
<tbody>
<tr class="odd">
<td><div class="content-wrapper">
<div class="office-container">
<div data-id="$attachmentObj">

</div>
<div class="container-menu-butttons">
<div class="companion-edit-button-placeholder" data-template-name="companionEditButon" data-linked-resource-id="435325189" data-linked-resource-container-id="435325187">

</div>
</div>
<div class="office-document">
<div>
<h1 id="recording-jmeter-script-using-blazemeter-chrome-extension-and-creating-jmeter-load-test" style="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; page-break-inside:avoid; page-break-after:avoid; line-height:108%; font-size:20pt">Recording Jmeter script using Blazemeter chrome extension and creating Jmeter load test</h1>
<p>What is Blazemeter Chrome Extension?</p>
<p>It record Selenium and HTTP traffic to create a load and functional tests in less than 10 minutes (Apache JMeter Compatible).</p>
<p>BlazeMeter Chrome extension enables you to - Record. Browse. Upload. Run.</p>
<p>The Chrome extension records all of the HTTP/S requests and actual user interactions that your browser sends, creates a synced JMeter and Selenium scripts, and automatically uploads it to BlazeMeter, where you can execute it with a single click. No need to install JMeter nor Selenium to record or run your performance test, the Chrome extension will create the JMeter and Selenium scripts automatically.</p>
<p>The extension will also allow you to debug and test your recorded Selenium session on your local Chrome browser.</p>
<p>By using JMeter locally, you can debug and enhance the JMX file create by the Chrome Extension to insure your script is ready to go.</p>
<p>How to download Blazemeter Chrome Extension?</p>
<p>Go to Chrome Web store and search for “Blazemeter” extension</p>
<p><br />
</p>
<p>Add the following extension to Chrome:</p>
<p><img src="plugins/servlet/benryanconversion" width="971" height="315" /></p>
<p><br />
</p>
<p>How to Record Jmeter API Load Test scripts using Blazemeter Chrome Extension?</p>
<p>Click on the “Blazemeter” extension in the Chrome browser:</p>
<p><img src="plugins/servlet/benryanconversion" width="338" height="363" /></p>
<p>Enter the name of the test and click on record button, it will start recording the API calls made at the backend</p>
<p>You can add Test Step name while recording your test</p>
<p><br />
</p>
<p>Click on Stop button once you finish recording the test</p>
<p><img src="plugins/servlet/benryanconversion" width="377" height="224" /></p>
<p>How to edit recorded API Load Test scripts using Blazemeter Chrome Extension?</p>
<p>Click on the “Blazemeter” extension in the Chrome browser again</p>
<p>Click on “Edit your script” button to see the recorded API calls and to modify them</p>
<p>It will open the Editor window with all the recorded API Calls</p>
<p><br />
</p>
<p>In this window, we can edit the script like Insert, Remove the calls</p>
<p><img src="plugins/servlet/benryanconversion" width="877" height="372" /></p>
<p>How to Use Recorded API scripts in Jmeter?</p>
<p>Once we have the final script, we can download it in .JMX format for JMETER (NOTE: To download .JMX file, you must create an account in Blazemeter and must be signed in, Creating account is simple you just need to enter Email and Password)</p>
<p>.JMX file can be downloaded in following ways:</p>
<ol type="1">
<li>Click on the .JMX button in the header of Editor window</li>
<li>Click on Blazemeter plugin and click on Download the recording button <img src="plugins/servlet/benryanconversion" width="49" height="44" /> and then select the type of script you want to download (.JMX) and click Save</li>
</ol>
<p>Open JMETER and import the .JMX file</p>
<p>Blazemeter will create complete test with all the required Config. Elements like HTTP Header Manager, HTT Cookie Manager Etc.</p>
<p>All the recorded API`s will be displayed under Thread Group</p>
<p><img src="plugins/servlet/benryanconversion" width="250" height="190" /></p>
<p>Click on Thread Group and configure the number of users by entering value in “Number of Threads” field:</p>
<p><img src="plugins/servlet/benryanconversion" width="251" height="169" /></p>
<p><span style="width:36pt; display:inline-block"></span><span style="width:36pt; display:inline-block"></span></p>
<p>After this step we can add the assertion steps to verify results and Listener steps to view reports in Jmeter Thread Group and Run our test by clicking on Play button.</p>
<p><br />
</p>
<p>Adding Assertion step to verify results:</p>
<p><span style="width:36pt; display:inline-block"></span><span style="width:36pt; display:inline-block"></span><img src="plugins/servlet/benryanconversion" width="621" height="595" /></p>
<p><span style="width:36pt; display:inline-block"></span><span style="width:36pt; display:inline-block"></span><br />
</p>
</div>
<br />

<div>
<p>Adding Listener step to view results:</p>
<p><span style="width:36pt; display:inline-block"></span><img src="plugins/servlet/benryanconversion" width="707" height="799" /></p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

</div>

  

  

  

  

  

  

</div>

</div>
